The Agent in Pre-emption: Authority and Limitations
Hanafi rulings on the agent for pre-emption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of agency in pre-emption, identify the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the need for opponent's consent, and apply the rules concerning the agent's waiver and the effect of the buyer's claims of waiver.

Core Idea
The agent for pre-emption is a litigant; the buyer's claim of waiver against the principal is not accepted.

The Hanafi school permits the shafi'i (pre-emptor) to appoint an agent to handle his pre-emption case. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rules: the agent can demand, waive, and litigate, but there are important nuances. Abu Hanifa requires the opponent's consent for agency, while the Sahibayn do not. The buyer's claim that the principal waived is not accepted against the agent. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly applying pre-emption law in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The appointment of an agent by the shafi'i to demand pre-emption. What is the ruling? The Hanafi school considers it valid (sahih), but with a disagreement on whether the opponent's consent is necessary.
The act involves both purchase and litigation, for which agency is generally valid.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that agency for pre-emption is not valid without the consent of the opponent (the buyer). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it is valid without consent. Note the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the agent's demand may be rejected if the buyer objects.
The mufta bihi position follows the Sahibayn for ease of transaction.
3
Analyze the buyer's claim of waiver
If the buyer claims that the shafi'i has waived his pre-emption, the text rules that such a claim is not accepted when the agent is making the demand. The agent is the representative, and the buyer's assertion is against the principal's right.
The text compares this to the agent for debt collection: a debtor's claim of discharge is not accepted against the agent.
4
Examine the analogy (qiyas) to debt collection
The ruling is derived by analogy to agency in debt collection. In that case, if the debtor claims the principal has discharged him, the debtor must still pay the agent, and then the agent swears the principal. Similarly, in pre-emption, the buyer must hand over the property to the agent, who then swears the principal.
This analogy shows that the agent's authority is independent of the principal's alleged waiver.
5
Distinguish the agent's authority to waive
If the agent himself waives the pre-emption, the text distinguishes: waiver before a judge (qadi) is valid, but outside court, according to the Sahibayn, it is not. However, Abu Yusuf allows it even outside court. The agent's waiver in court is effective because the judge can verify the agent's authority.
This highlights the importance of judicial context for certain acts of the agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوكيل بطلب الشفعة خصم لأن الأخذ بالشفعة يتضمن للشراء والخصومة والوكيل بهما جائز إلا عند أبي حنيفة لأنه لا يصح إلا برضا الخصم، وعندهما جائز بغير رضا الخصم. ولو طلب وكيل الشفيع فقال المشتري قد سلم الشفيع لا يقبل قوله، وكذلك لو أراد يمينه أنه يفرط في طلب الشفعة ولكن يؤمر بتسليم الدار إلى الوكيل ثم يتبع الموكل ويستحلفه وصار كالوكيل بقبض الدين إذا ادعى المديون الإبراء من الموكل فإنه يؤمر بدفع الدين للوكيل ثم يتبع الموكل ويستحلفه على ذلك، ولو سلم الوكيل الشفعة أو أقر بالتسليم عند القاضي جاز تسليمه لأن من ملك الأخذ بالشفعة ملك التسليم كما في الأب والوصي ولا يجوز عند غير القاضي عندهما. وقال أبو يوسف : يجوز بناء على أن الوكيل إذا أقر على موكله بالتسليم في غير مجلس الحاكم يقبل لما يأتي في الوكالة للدار شفيعان فوكلا رجلاً فقال سلمت شفعة أحدهما ولم يبين أيهما هو وقال أطلب الآخر ليس له ذلك حتى يبين لأن القاضي يحتاج إلى أن يقضي بالشفعة لأحدهما وبالتسليم على الآخر ولا يمكنه ذلك إلا بعد البيان. وكل الشفيع لأن الأخذ بالشفعة شراء والواحد لا يصلح وكيلاً بالشراء من الجانبين، وكذلك لو وكل البائع استحساناً لأنه أخذاً نفسه فيؤدي إلى التضاد الحقوق إن كان المبيع في يده، وبعد التسليم يصير . ساعياً في نقض ما قد تم من جهته لأنه بأخذه ينفسخ العقد بينه وبين المشتري ولا يجوز لأحد المتعاقدين السعي في نقض ما تم به . وكله بأن يأخذ الشفعة بكذا وكان المشتري اشترى بأكثر لا يأخذ لأن الوكيل بالشفعة وكيل بالشراء والوكيل بالشراء لا يملك الشراء بأكثر مما بين له الموكل من الثمن، وكذلك لو قال اشترها من فلان فاشتراها من غيره لا ينفذ لأنه خالف فخاصمه في أخرى ليس له ذلك إلا إذا عمم في التوكيل لأن الوكيل بشراء دار بعينها لا يملك شراء دار أخرى. لو طلب المشتري من الوكيل بطلب الشفعة أن يكف عنه مدة على أنه على خصومته وشفعته جاز لأن الشفيع لو أخر وأمهل المشتري بعد الإشهاد بدون طلبه جاز فكذلك بطلب وكيله، ولا تبطل بموت الوكيل وتبطل بموت الموكل ولحاقه بدار الحرب مرتداً لأن الحق ثابت للموكل الشفعة لا للوكيل. وفي المنتقى : ولو وكل رجلاً بطلب كل حق له وبالخصومة والقبض ليس له أن يطلب شفعته لأن الشفعة شراء والوكيل بالخصومة لا يملك الشراء وله أن يقبض شفعة قد قضى بها .
The agent for demanding pre-emption is a litigant because taking by pre-emption involves purchase and litigation, and agency for both is permissible except according to Abu Hanifa, because it is not valid except with the consent of the opponent. According to them (the two students), it is valid without the opponent's consent. If the agent demands and the buyer says, 'The shafi'i has waived,' his words are not accepted. Similarly, if he wants him to swear that his right is lost, but he is ordered to hand over the house to the agent, then the agent follows the principal and asks him to swear. It is like the agent for collecting debt: if the debtor claims discharge from the principal, the debtor is ordered to pay the debt to the agent, then the agent follows the principal and asks him to swear regarding that. If the agent waives the pre-emption or acknowledges waiver before the judge, his waiver is valid because whoever has the right to take by pre-emption has the right to waive, like the father and executor, but it is not valid before a non-judge according to them (the two). Abu Yusuf said: It is valid based on the principle that if the agent acknowledges waiver on behalf of his principal outside the court, it is accepted, as will come in the chapter of agency. For a house with two shafi'is, they appoint one man as agent, and he says, 'I waived the pre-emption of one of them,' without specifying which, and says, 'I demand the other,' he does not have that right until he specifies, because the judge needs to adjudicate pre-emption for one and waiver against the other, and that is not possible without specification. One appointed the shafi'i because taking by pre-emption is a purchase, and one person is not fit to be an agent for purchase from both sides, similarly if the seller appoints, based on istihsan, because it leads to conflicting rights if the sold item is in his hand, and after delivery, he becomes a party seeking to undo what has been completed from his side, because by his taking, the contract between him and the buyer is rescinded, and it is not permissible for one of the two contracting parties to work towards undoing what has been completed. If he appoints him to take by pre-emption for a certain price and the buyer bought for more, he does not take, because the agent for pre-emption is an agent for purchase, and the agent for purchase does not have the authority to buy for more than what the principal specified. Similarly, if he says, 'Buy it from so-and-so,' and he buys it from someone else, it is not valid because he violated the terms. So he cannot litigate in another matter unless the agency is general. If the buyer asks the agent for pre-emption to refrain for a period on the basis that he still has his claim and pre-emption, it is permissible, because if the shafi'i delays and gives the buyer time after the declaration without his request, it is valid, and similarly through his agent. It is not invalidated by the death of the agent, but it is invalidated by the death of the principal and his joining the abode of war as an apostate, because the right of pre-emption is established for the principal, not for the agent. In al-Muntaqa: If a man appoints an agent for all his rights, litigation, and collection, he does not have the right to demand his pre-emption, because pre-emption is a purchase, and the agent for litigation does not have the authority to purchase, but he may collect a pre-emption that has been adjudged.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage deals extensively with the role of the agent (wakil) in pre-emption. The Hanafi school generally allows the shafi'i to appoint an agent to demand pre-emption, though there is a difference: Abu Hanifa requires the consent of the opponent (the buyer) for the agent to act, whereas Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) do not require it. This is because pre-emption involves both a purchase and litigation, and agency for both is valid. The passage then discusses cases where the buyer claims that the shafi'i has already waived the right; such a claim is not accepted when the agent is present, because the agent is the representative, and the buyer's assertion is against the principal's right. The agent's own waiver in court is valid, but outside court, according to the Sahibayn, it is not; Abu Yusuf allows it. The text also covers the scenario of two shafi'is appointing one agent: if the agent waives for one without specifying which, he must specify, otherwise the judge cannot decide. The passage also touches on the agent's authority in terms of price: the agent cannot take pre-emption for a higher price than specified, nor can he buy from a different seller unless authorized generally. Finally, the agent's authority ends with the principal's death or apostasy, but not with the agent's death. The ruling from al-Muntaqa clarifies that a general agent for all rights does not automatically have authority over pre-emption, as it is a purchase.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by the shafi'i to handle his pre-emption case.
خصومة (khusuma): Litigation or legal dispute, which the agent can undertake.
إبراء (ibra'): Discharge or release from a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if the agent for pre-emption demands the property and the buyer claims the shafi'i waived, what is the ruling?
A) The agent's demand is dismissed.
B) The agent must produce the shafi'i in court.
C) The buyer's claim is not accepted, and the agent continues.
D) The agent must swear that the shafi'i did not waive.

Key Takeaway
The agent for pre-emption has independent authority; the buyer's claim of waiver is not accepted against the agent.

Effect of Misinformation on Waiver of Pre-emption
Rulings on waiver of pre-emption after misinformation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a pre-emptor's waiver is invalid if he was misinformed about the price, and distinguish when the waiver stands despite a change in the nature of the price.

Core Idea
A waiver based on ignorance of the true price is void; pre-emption revives unless the value is equivalent in non-measurables.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical nuance in pre-emption (shuf'a) law: when does a pre-emptor's waiver remain valid if he was misled about the price? The key principle is that the pre-emptor's consent is conditioned on accurate knowledge. However, the ruling depends on whether the price is in measurable/weighable items or in goods (urud). We will walk through the scenarios and the Hanafi proof based on qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for a valid waiver
The pre-emptor must have full knowledge of the price to validly waive. If he is told a higher price and waives, but discovers a lower price, his waiver is based on ignorance and is void.
The basis (sabab) of waiver is the high price; when that disappears, the waiver collapses.
2
Distinguish between measurable/weighable items and goods
For items sold by measure (makil) or weight (mawzun), a change in the type of item (e.g., wheat vs. barley) also revives pre-emption because the pre-emptor's desire varies with the specific type. For goods (urud), only the value matters; if the value remains the same, no revival.
Goods are valued in dirhams/dinars; if the new goods have equal value, there is no practical difference.
3
Apply the rule to mixed scenarios
If the pre-emptor was told the price is goods but it turns out to be measurable items, or vice versa, he retains pre-emption because the basis of valuation changes. Similarly, if the type of measurable item changes, pre-emption revives.
This is because the obligation in measurable items is to deliver that specific type, not its value.
4
Address the critique from al-Nihayah
The author of al-Nihayah argues that the restriction 'worth a thousand or more' is unnecessary because the absolute ruling from al-Mabsut and al-Idah states that if the discovered price is less, waiver is invalid regardless of amount. The response defends the restriction as beneficial in specific cases.
This shows the dynamic nature of Hanafi legal reasoning; refinements are made to avoid misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن قيل للشفيع أنها بيعت بألف فسلم ثم علم أنها بيعت بأقل أو ببرأ وشعير قيمته ألف أو أكثر فله الشفعة لأن تسليمه كان لاستكثار الثمن أو لتعذر الجنس ظاهراً فإذا تبين له خلاف ذلك كان له الأخذ للتيسير وعدم الرضا على تقدير أن الثمن غيره لأن الرغبة في الأخذ تختلف باختلاف الثمن قدراً وجنساً، فإذا سلم على بعض الوجوه لا يلزم منه التسليم في الوجوه كلها ، وكذا كل موزون أو مكيل أو عددي متفاوت بخلاف ما إذا علم أنها بيعت بعروض قيمتها ألف أو أكثر لأن الواجب فيه القيمة وهي دراهم أو دنانير يظهر فيه التيسير فلا يكون له الأخذ وكذا لو أخبر أن الثمن عروض كالثياب والعبيد فظهر أنه مكيل أو موزون أو أخبر أن الثمن مكيل أو موزون فظهر من خلاف جنسه من المكيل والموزون فهو على شفعته لما ذكرنا وإن ظهر أنه جنس آخر من العروض قيمته مثل قيمة الذي بلغه أو ظهر أنه ذهب أو فضة قدره مثل قيمة ذلك فلا شفعة له لعدم الفائدة لأن في غير المكيل والموزون الواجب القيمة فلا يظهر التفاوت . قال صاحب النهاية : تقييده بقوله قيمته ألف أو أكثر غير مفيد فإنه لو كان قيمته أقل من ألف فتسلمه باطل لإطلاق المبسوط والإيضاح حيث قالا : ثم ظهر له مكيل أو موزون فهو على شفعته وأجيب بأنه مفيد لأنه
The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'If it is said to the shafi'i that it was sold for a thousand, and he waives, then he learns that it was sold for less, or for wheat and barley worth a thousand or more, then he has pre-emption, because his waiver was due to the high price or the absence of that type apparently. When it becomes clear to him contrary to that, he may take because of the ease and the lack of consent on the basis that the price is different. Because desire to take differs with difference in price in quantity and type. If he waives for some aspects, it does not necessitate waiver for all aspects. Similarly, every weight-based, measure-based, or count-based item that varies. Unlike the case if he knew it was sold for goods worth a thousand or more, because the obligatory (in such goods) is value, which is dirhams or dinars, and ease is apparent, so he does not have the right to take. Similarly, if he was informed that the price is goods like clothes and slaves, then it appears to be a measured or weighed item, or he was informed that the price is a measured or weighed item, then it appears to be from a different type of measured or weighed items, then he holds his pre-emption due to what we mentioned. And if it appears that it is another type of goods whose value is equal to the value of what he was informed, or it appears that it is gold or silver of a quantity equal to that value, then he has no pre-emption because of the lack of benefit. Because in non-measured or weighed items, the obligation is value, so no disparity appears.' The author of al-Nihayah said: 'His restriction to 'its value a thousand or more' is not beneficial, because if its value is less than a thousand, his waiver would be invalid due to the absolute statements of al-Mabsut and al-Idah, where they said: 'Then it appears to him to be measured or weighed, so he holds his pre-emption.' And it was answered that it is beneficial because...'
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical scenario in pre-emption law: when the shafi'i waives his right after being informed that the property was sold for a certain price, but later discovers the actual price was lower or of a different type. The core principle is that the waiver is only valid if based on correct information. If the shafi'i thought the price was high and so waived, but discovers it was low, his waiver is deemed ineffective because the basis (sabab) of his waiver was the high price, which no longer holds. Similarly, if he thought the price was in a difficult-to-value type (like goods) but it turns out to be in specific items like wheat or barley (which are measurable), he may still claim pre-emption due to the change in ease of valuation. However, if the price was in goods and it turns out to be other goods of equal value, or gold/silver of equal value, his waiver stands because the value is the same and there is no practical difference. The passage also notes a critical nuance: for measurable (makil) and weighable (mawzun) items, the shafi'i's willingness to pay may depend on the specific type; thus, if the type changes, his waiver may be void. For non-measurable items, the value in gold/silver is the standard, so no change of type matters as long as the value is constant. The author of al-Nihayah critiques a restriction in the matn about 'value a thousand or more,' arguing that the absolute ruling from earlier texts is that if the discovered price is less, the waiver is invalid regardless. The response suggests the restriction is still meaningful in certain cases.

Key Terms
مكيل (makil): Items sold by measure (e.g., grains). In pre-emption, a change in type of makil revives the right because the pre-emptor's desire is specific to the commodity.
موزون (mawzun): Items sold by weight (e.g., metals, some foods). Same rule as makil.
عروض (urud): Goods other than gold, silver, or foodstuffs; non-monetary items. In pre-emption, if the price is in urud and changes to another type of urud of equal value, the waiver stands because the obligation is value.
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Pre-emption right – the right of a co-owner or neighbour to buy property that has been sold to an outsider, by paying the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A pre-emptor is told the property was sold for 1000 dirhams, and he waives. Later he discovers it was sold for 1000 dirhams worth of barley (a measurable item). What is the ruling?
A) He has no pre-emption because the value is the same.
B) He has pre-emption because the type changed to a measurable item.
C) He may take only if the barley is worth more than 1000.
D) His waiver is valid regardless.

Key Takeaway
A pre-emptor's waiver is invalid if he was misinformed about the price in quantity or type, except when the discovered price is equivalent in value for non-measurable items.

Agency in Pre-emption: Limitations on Representation
Examines agency rules in shuf'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid agency in pre-emption and identify prohibitions on representation of conflicting parties.

Core Idea
One agent cannot represent both sides in pre-emption; the agent cannot exceed the principal's price limit.

This lesson explores the rules of agency (wakalah) as applied to the right of pre-emption (shuf'a). The Hanafi school sets clear boundaries to prevent conflict of interest and to ensure that the agent acts within the principal's specified terms. Understanding these limitations is crucial for correctly executing or challenging pre-emption claims through representatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties in a shuf'a scenario
Recognize the shafi' (pre-emptor), the buyer, and the seller, each with distinct interests.
2
Understand the conflict of interest rule
A single agent cannot represent both the buyer and the shafi' simultaneously, as pre-emption is a purchase and requires undivided loyalty.
The text explicitly states: 'وكل الشفيع لأن الأخذ بالشفعة شراء والواحد لا يصلح وكيلاً بالشراء من المشتري'
3
Recognize the agent's price and property limitations
The agent must act within the specified price and cannot purchase a different property than the one designated.
Exceeding the price or buying from a different seller renders the agency ineffective.
4
Note the effects of death or apostasy on agency
The agency terminates upon the death or apostasy of the principal, but not upon the death of the agent.
The text differentiates: 'ولا تبطل بموت الوكيل وتبطل بموت الموكل ولحاقه بدار الحرب مرتداً'
5
Distinguish general litigation agency from specific pre-emption agency
A general agent for litigation cannot demand pre-emption unless explicitly authorized, because pre-emption is a purchase, not a mere legal claim.
The passage from al-Muntaqa clarifies this distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة باب ما تبطل به الشفعة
أو ببرأ وشعير قيمته ألف أو أكثر فله الشفعة ولو بان أنها بيعت بدنانير قيمتها ألف فلا
أحدهما ولم يبين أيهما هو وقال أطلب الآخر ليس له ذلك حتى يبين لأن القاضي يحتاج إلى أن يقضي بالشفعة لأحدهما وبالتسليم على الآخر ولا يمكنه ذلك إلا بعد البيان. وكل الشفيع لأن الأخذ بالشفعة شراء والواحد لا يصلح وكيلاً بالشراء من المشتري فأخذها لم يصح يصير في الجانبين، وكذلك لو وكل البائع استحساناً لأنه أخذاً نفسه فيؤدي إلى التضاد الحقوق إن كان المبيع في يده، وبعد التسليم يصير . ساعياً في نقض ما قد تم من جهته لأنه بأخذه ينفسخ العقد بينه وبين المشتري ولا يجوز لأحد المتعاقدين السعي في نقض ما تم به . وكله بأن يأخذ الشفعة بكذا وكان المشتري اشترى بأكثر لا يأخذ لأن الوكيل بالشفعة وكيل بالشراء والوكيل بالشراء لا يملك الشراء بأكثر مما بين له الموكل من الثمن، وكذلك لو قال اشترها من فلان فاشتراها من غيره لا ينفذ لأنه خالف فخاصمه في أخرى ليس له ذلك إلا إذا عمم في التوكيل لأن الوكيل بشراء دار بعينها لا يملك شراء دار أخرى. لو طلب المشتري من الوكيل بطلب الشفعة أن يكف عنه مدة على أنه على خصومته وشفعته جاز لأن الشفيع لو أخر وأمهل المشتري بعد الإشهاد بدون طلبه جاز فكذلك بطلب وكيله، ولا تبطل بموت الوكيل وتبطل بموت الموكل ولحاقه بدار الحرب مرتداً لأن الحق ثابت للموكل الشفعة لا للوكيل. وفي المنتقى : ولو وكل رجلاً بطلب كل حق له وبالخصومة والقبض ليس له أن يطلب شفعته لأن الشفعة شراء والوكيل بالخصومة لا يملك الشراء وله أن يقبض شفعة قد
قضى بها .
Book of Pre-emption: Chapter on What Invalidates Pre-emption. Or with barley and wheat whose value is a thousand or more, he has the pre-emption. And if it appears that it was sold for dinars worth a thousand, then no... one of them and he did not specify which one it is, and he said: I seek the other, he does not have that until he specifies, because the judge needs to decree pre-emption for one and delivery to the other, and that is not possible except after specification. And the agency of the pre-emptor because taking pre-emption is a purchase, and one person does not suffice as agent for purchase from the buyer, so his taking it is not valid; he becomes in both sides. Similarly, if the seller appoints an agent, by istihsan, because it is taking himself, leading to contradiction of rights if the sold item is in his hand. And after delivery, he becomes striving to undo what has been completed from his side, because by his taking, the contract is annulled between him and the buyer, and it is not permissible for either party to strive to undo what has been completed by him. And he appointed him to take the pre-emption for such price, and the buyer had bought for more, he does not take, because the agent for pre-emption is an agent for purchase, and the agent for purchase does not have the right to purchase for more than what the principal specified as price. Similarly, if he said: Buy it from so-and-so, and he bought it from someone else, it is not effective because he violated. So he litigates against him in another, he does not have that unless the authorization is general, because the agent for purchase of a specific house does not have the right to purchase another house. If the buyer asks the agent for demanding pre-emption to refrain from him for a period on the condition that he is upon his litigation and his pre-emption, it is permissible, because if the pre-emptor delayed and gave respite to the buyer after testimony without his request, it is permissible, so likewise by request of his agent. And it is not invalidated by the death of the agent, and it is invalidated by the death of the principal and his joining the Abode of War as an apostate, because the right is established for the principal, not for the agent. And in al-Muntaqa: If he appointed a man to demand every right of his, and for litigation and receipt, he does not have the right to demand his pre-emption, because pre-emption is a purchase, and the agent for litigation does not have the right to purchase; but he has the right to receive a pre-emption that has been decreed.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the rules of agency (wakalah) in the context of shuf'a (pre-emption). It begins by noting that if a shafi' (pre-emptor) is told that the property was sold for a certain price or with specific goods, and later learns otherwise, various rulings apply. However, the main focus here is on the validity of appointments. The text explains that a single person cannot act as agent for both the buyer and the shafi' simultaneously, as that would involve conflicting interests. Similarly, if the seller appoints an agent, it is permitted by istihsan because the agent is acting on his own behalf. After delivery of the property, the shafi' cannot act to undo the contract. If a shafi' appoints an agent to take the pre-emption for a specified price, the agent cannot take it for a higher price. If the agent buys from a different seller, the purchase is invalid. If the buyer asks the agent to delay, it is permissible. The agency is not invalidated by the death of the agent but is invalidated by the death of the principal or his apostasy. Finally, a general agent for litigation does not have the authority to demand pre-emption, as pre-emption is a purchase.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): The right of pre-emption; the right of a co-owner or neighbour to purchase a property that has been sold to a third party, under specific conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a shafi' appoints an agent to take pre-emption for a price of 1000, but the property was actually bought by the buyer for 1200, can the agent take the pre-emption for 1200?
A) Yes, because the agent has authority to negotiate.
B) No, because the agent cannot buy for more than the principal specified.
C) Yes, if the agent believes it is a good deal.
D) No, but the principal can ratify.

Key Takeaway
Agency in pre-emption is strictly limited: the agent cannot represent conflicting parties and must act within the principal's specified terms; violation invalidates the action.

Misrepresentation of Price and Goods in Pre-emption
Detailed rulings on when shafi' retains right despite misinformation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a shafi' may retain shuf'a after surrendering based on incorrect information about the price or type of goods, and apply the governing principle to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Surrender of shuf'a is void if the shafi' was misinformed and the truth makes the transaction more favourable.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author details the effect of misrepresentation of the price or goods (thaman/muthaman) on the validity of the shafi''s surrender (taslim). The core legal principle is that surrender is only binding if the shafi' had full knowledge of the actual terms. If he surrendered because he believed the price was too high or the goods were unavailable, and later discovers the price was lower or the goods were obtainable, his surrender is invalid and he retains the right of pre-emption. The passage explores various scenarios to illustrate how this principle applies across different categories of property and price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The passage starts: if the shafi' surrenders thinking the price is high but later finds it was lower, or the goods were different but easier, his surrender is invalid. This is because his intent was conditional on that specific information.
Key terms: لاستكثار الثمن (considering price too high) and لتعذر الجنس (difficulty of the species).
2
Distinguish between price in value versus price in kind
If the price was in dirhams/dinars (value) and the truth is the same value, no benefit, surrender valid. But if the goods were of a type where variation matters (weighed/measured/counted), the surrender is void if the truth is easier.
See distinction between موزون (weighed) / مكيل (measured) versus عروض (goods).
3
Apply to variation in buyer identity and partial sales
If the buyer's identity was misrepresented, surrender is void. Similarly, if informed of a partial sale but it turns out to be the whole, surrender void; if informed of whole but turns out half, surrender valid because he disliked the whole more.
This uses reasoning of أولى (priority).
4
Handle post-surrender price reduction or addition of goods
If after surrender the seller reduces the price, or adds an ancillary item, the shafi' may retract because the actual price share for the property is less.
Surrender is contingent on the contract as finalized.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar
Zufar holds that the shafi' always retains the right regardless of price variation, while Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on type. The preferred view is Imam's.
Marked as وهو قول الإمام.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن قيل للشفيع أنها بيعت بألف فسلم ثم علم أنها بيعت بأقل أو ببرأ وشعير قيمته ألف أو أكثر فله (الشفعة لأن تسليمه كان لاستكثار الثمن أو لتعذر الجنس ظاهراً فإذا تبين له خلاف ذلك كان له الأخذ للتيسير وعدم الرضا على تقدير أن الثمن غيره لأن الرغبة في الأخذ تختلف باختلاف الثمن قدراً وجنساً، فإذا سلم على بعض الوجوه لا يلزم منه التسليم في الوجوه كلها ، وكذا كل موزون أو مكيل أو عددي متفاوت بخلاف ما إذا علم أنها بيعت بعروض قيمتها ألف أو أكثر لأن الواجب فيه القيمة وهي دراهم أو دنانير يظهر فيه التيسير فلا يكون له الأخذ وكذا لو أخبر أن الثمن عروض كالثياب والعبيد فظهر أنه مكيل أو موزون أو أخبر أن الثمن مكيل أو موزون فظهر من خلاف جنسه من المكيل والموزون فهو على شفعته لما ذكرنا وإن ظهر أنه جنس آخر من العروض قيمته مثل قيمة الذي بلغه أو ظهر أنه ذهب أو فضة قدره مثل قيمة ذلك فلا شفعة له لعدم الفائدة لأن في غير المكيل والموزون الواجب القيمة فلا يظهر التفاوت . قال صاحب النهاية : تقييده بقوله قيمته ألف أو أكثر غير مفيد فإنه لو كان قيمته أقل من ألف فتسلمه باطل لإطلاق المبسوط والإيضاح حيث قالا : ثم ظهر له مكيل أو موزون فهو على شفعته وأجيب بأنه مفيد لأنه .
شفعة له وإن قيل له أن المشتري فلان فسلم ثم ظهر أنه غيره فله الشفعة وإن باعها إلا إذا علم أن الشفعة لا تبطل إذا ظهر أنه أكثر علم بطريق الأولى أنها لا تبطل إذا ظهر أنه أقل . وفي المحيط : ولو بلغه أن الثمن عبد فظهر أنه جارية ينظر إن كان قيمة الجارية كقيمة العبد أو أكثر بطلت وإن كان أقل من قيمة العبد لا تبطل فهو كما لو أخبر بالثمن ألف وظهر أقل. ولو أخبر أن الثمن ألف درهم فسلم فإذا هو مائة دينار لم يذكره في الأصل أيضاً. وذكر الكرخي ينظر؛ إن كان قيمة الدنانير ألف درهم أو أكثر صح التسليم وهو قول شيخ الإسلام؛ كذا في التجريد. وروي عن زفر له في الوجهين الشفعة وهو قول الإمام. ولو أخبر أنه باع نصفها فسلم ثم علم أنه باع كلها فله الشفعة لأن من رغب عن البعض لعيب الشركة لا يكون راغباً عن الكل وليس فيه عيب ولو أخبر أنه باع الكل فسلم ثم علم أنه باع نصفها بطلت شفعته لأن من رغب عنها وليس بها عيب الشركة كان راغباً عنها وبها عيب الشركة بالطريق الأولى. قالوا وتأويلها أن يكون ثمن النصف ثمن الكل فلو أخبر أنه باع الكل بألف ثم علم أنه باع النصف بخمسمائة فإنه يجب أن يكون على شفعته لأنه إذا رغب في الأول لعجزه عن الألف فلا يكون راغباً عن الخمسمائة ولو أخبر أنها بيعت بألف فسلم الشفيع الشفعة ثم حط البائع عن المشتري شيئاً من الثمن وقبل الحط فله الشفعة لأنه يلتحق بأصل العقد فصار كما لو أخبر أنها بيعت بألف فظهر أنها بيعت بأقل . منه، ولو زاد البائع مشتري الدار عليها عبداً أو أمة بعد ما سلم الشفيع الشفعة كان للشفيع أن يأخذ الدار بحصتها من الثمن لأنه تبين أن حصة الدار من الثمن أقل، ولو قضى القاضي له بالشفعة ولم يعلم بالثمن ثم علم فله الخيار لأن رضاه بالأخذ إنما يتم إذا علم بالثمن ا هـ . . وفي التجريد وغيره أخبر أن الثمن عبد أو جارية فظهر أنه مكيل أو موزون فهو على شفعته ا هـ .
The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'If it is said to the pre-emptor that it was sold for a thousand, and he surrendered, then he learned that it was sold for less, or for barley and wheat whose value is a thousand or more, he has the pre-emption because his surrender was due to considering the price too high or the difficulty of the species apparently. When the contrary becomes clear to him, he may take due to ease and lack of consent on the assumption that the price was something else, because desire to take differs with difference in price in quantity and kind. If he surrenders in some aspects, it does not necessitate surrender in all aspects. Likewise, every weighed, measured, or counted item that varies, contrary to if he knows that it was sold for goods worth a thousand or more, because what is obligatory therein is value, which is dirhams or dinars, where ease appears, so he does not take. Similarly, if he was informed that the price was goods like clothes and slaves, but it appears to be measured or weighed; or he was informed that the price was measured or weighed, and it appears to be different in kind of measured or weighed, he is upon his pre-emption for the reason we mentioned. If it appears that it was another kind of goods, its value like the value of what was reported, or it appears that it was gold or silver of like value, then no pre-emption for him due to lack of benefit, because in other than measured/weighed, the value is obligatory, so no variation appears. The author of al-Nihayah said: His restriction to 'value a thousand or more' is not useful, because if its value is less than a thousand, his surrender is invalid due to the absolute statement of al-Mabsut and al-Idah, where they said: Then it appears to him as measured or weighed, he is upon his pre-emption. And the answer is that it is useful because... He has pre-emption, and if it is said to him that the buyer is so-and-so, and he surrendered, then it appeared that it was someone else, he has the pre-emption. And if he sold it except if he knows... that the pre-emption does not become void if it appears that it is more, he knows by priority that it does not become void if it appears that it is less. In al-Muhit: If he was informed that the price was a slave, but it appears to be a female slave, it is to be considered: if the value of the female slave is like the value of the slave or more, the surrender is void? [text unclear] and if it is less than the value of the slave, it does not become void. So it is like if he was informed that the price is a thousand and it appears less. And if he was informed that the price was a thousand dirhams and he surrendered, then it turned out to be a hundred dinars, he did not mention it in the original either. Al-Karkhi mentioned: it is considered; if the value of the dinars is a thousand dirhams or more, the surrender is valid, and it is the saying of Shaykh al-Islam. Likewise in al-Tajrid. And it is narrated from Zufr that he has the pre-emption in both aspects, and it is the saying of the Imam. And if he was informed that he sold half of it, and he surrendered, then he learned that he sold all of it, he has the pre-emption, because one who dislikes a part due to the defect of partnership does not dislike the whole, and there is no defect in it. And if he was informed that he sold the whole, and he surrendered, then he learned that he sold half, his pre-emption becomes void, because one who dislikes it and there is no defect of partnership in it, he dislikes it, and with the defect of partnership, it is all the more reason. They said: Its interpretation is that the price of the half is the price of the whole. So if he was informed that he sold the whole for a thousand, then he learned that he sold the half for five hundred, then he must be upon his pre-emption, because if he disliked the first due to inability to pay a thousand, he does not dislike the five hundred. And if he was informed that it was sold for a thousand, and the pre-emptor surrendered the pre-emption, then the seller reduced something of the price for the buyer and he accepted the reduction, he has the pre-emption because it attaches to the original contract, so it becomes as if he was informed that it was sold for a thousand and it appeared that it was sold for less. From it: And if the seller of the house adds to it a slave or female slave after the pre-emptor surrendered the pre-emption, then the pre-emptor may take the house with its portion of the price, because it becomes clear that the share of the house from the price is less. And if the judge decreed pre-emption for him and he did not know the price, then he learned, he has the option, because his consent to take is only complete when he knows the price. End quote. In al-Tajrid and others: He was informed that the price was a slave or female slave, and it appeared that it was measured or weighed, he is upon his pre-emption. End.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq's commentary deals with scenarios where the shafi' (pre-emptor) surrenders his right based on incorrect information about the price or the type of goods involved in the sale. The core principle is that surrender of shuf'a is conditional on full and accurate knowledge. If the shafi' surrenders because he believes the price is too high or the goods are unavailable, and later discovers the price was lower or the goods were of a type he could obtain, his surrender is invalid and he retains the right of pre-emption. The text distinguishes between different categories: if the price is in coins (dirhams/dinars) or valuable goods (urud), the rule differs. For weighed or measured items, the variation matters; for goods of equal value, no benefit, so no shuf'a. The text also discusses cases where the buyer's identity is misrepresented, or where only part of the property was sold. A reduction in price after surrender revives the shuf'a. If the seller adds an ancillary item, the shafi' can take the property at its reduced share. Throughout, the reasoning is based on the shafi''s presumed intent and the practical benefit of the transaction.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-taslim): Surrender of the right of pre-emption; the shafi' explicitly waives his claim.
المشتري (al-mushtari): The buyer; the person who purchases the property.
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): The right of pre-emption: a neighbor or co-owner may purchase property sold to a third party by paying the sale price.
الغبن/التغرير (al-taghrir): Misrepresentation or deception leading to a flawed consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A shafi' is told the property was sold for 1000 dirhams, surrenders, then learns it was sold for 500 dirhams. Which statement is correct according to the passage?
A) The surrender is valid and shuf'a is lost.
B) The surrender is invalid and the shafi' may still take with shuf'a.
C) The shafi' must pay the difference of 500 dirhams.
D) The surrender is invalid only if the goods type also changed.

Key Takeaway
Surrender of shuf'a is conditional on accurate knowledge; material misrepresentation of price or goods renders the surrender invalid, preserving the right of pre-emption.

Surrender of Shuf'a in Cases of Talji'a and Mistaken Identity
Rulings on surrender of shuf'a when the sale is fictitious or involves third-party agreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on surrender of shuf'a when the sale is a talji'a and apply it to scenarios involving options and mistaken buyer identity.

Core Idea
Surrender of shuf'a is final; subsequent acknowledgment of a fictitious sale does not revive the right.

In pre-emption (shuf'a), the right can be lost by surrender. But what if the sale was a sham (talji'a) designed to circumvent your right? The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: even if the sale is later proven to be a fiction, the surrender extinguishes the right permanently—with a few nuanced exceptions involving gifts and options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of surrender
The shafi' voluntarily gives up his right of pre-emption. This is a legal act with consequences.
Surrender can be explicit or implied.
2
Apply the ruling when talji'a is discovered after surrender
According to the text, even if the buyer and seller admit the sale was a talji'a, the surrender remains valid and the shafi' does not get his right back.
This is based on the principle that after surrender, no right remains.
3
Contrast with discovery before surrender
If the talji'a is discovered before the shafi' surrenders, his right remains and he can still claim shuf'a.
The text notes that this is different from the case after surrender.
4
Analyze the gift-disguised-as-sale scenario
If the shafi' surrenders in a gift with countervalue, and it turns out to be a sale, the surrender is final. But if the gift had no condition of countervalue, and the parties later agree it was a gift with countervalue, the shafi' retains shuf'a.
The key is the nature of the transaction at the time of surrender.
5
Examine the option case and intra-Hanafi difference
If the shafi' surrenders and later the buyer gives the seller an option to cancel within a day, Muhammad holds that the surrender is absolute and does not revive upon cancellation. Abu Yusuf holds that if the sale is rescinded, the shafi' gets his right back.
This is an ikhtilaf within the madhhab; the mufta bihi is not specified in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو بان أنها بيعت بدنانير قيمتها ألف فلا شفعة (له وهو قول أبي يوسف. وقد بينا المسألة بفروعها فيما تقدم. وفي المحيط : سلم الشفيع الشفعة فقال المشتري للبائع كان تلجئة لا يتجدد شفعته لأنه بعد ما سلم لم يبق له حق فصح إقرارهما بأن البيع تلجئة فكان فاسداً، ولو ثبت معاينة أن البيع تلجئة لا يتجدد للشفيع حق الشفعة بخلاف ما لو كان قبل التسلم لأن حق الشفيع ثبت من حيث الظاهر فإقرارهما يتضمن إبطال حقه فلا يقبل تسلم الشفيع في هبة بعوض فظهر أنه بيع لم تعد الشفعة، ولو سلم في هبة بغير شرط العوض ثم تصادقا أنه كان بشرط العوض فله الشفعة وفي النوادر ولو سلم الشفعة ثم جعل المشتري للبائع خيار يوم جاز فإن نقض البائع البيع في ذلك اليوم لا يتجدد للشفيع حق الشفعة؛ رواه ابن سماعة عن محمد، وروى ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف أن له الشفعة ا هـ .
قال رحمه الله : (وإن قيل له أن المشتري فلان فسلم ثم ظهر أنه غيره فله الشفعة) لتفاوت الناس في الأخلاق فمنهم من يرغب في معاشرته، ومنهم من يجتنب مخافة شره
The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And if it appears that it was sold for dinars worth a thousand, then no pre-emption for him.' This is the saying of Abu Yusuf. And we have explained the issue with its branches previously. And in al-Muhit: The pre-emptor surrendered the pre-emption, and the buyer said to the seller: it was a talji'a (fictitious sale), his pre-emption does not renew, because after he surrendered, no right remained for him, so their acknowledgment that the sale was talji'a is valid, so it was fasid. And if it is established by visual evidence that the sale was talji'a, the right of pre-emption does not renew for the pre-emptor, contrary to if it was before receiving, because the right of the pre-emptor was established from the apparent, so their acknowledgment entails invalidating his right, so it is not accepted. The pre-emptor surrendered in a gift with a countervalue, then it appeared that it was a sale, the pre-emption does not return. And if he surrendered in a gift without the condition of countervalue, then they both agreed that it was with a condition of countervalue, he has the pre-emption. And in al-Nawadir: If the pre-emptor surrendered the pre-emption, then the buyer gave the seller a one-day option, it is permissible. If the seller cancels the sale on that day, the right of pre-emption does not renew for the pre-emptor; this is narrated by Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad. And Ibn Sama'a narrated from Abu Yusuf that he has the pre-emption. End quote. The author said: 'And if it is said to him that the buyer is so-and-so, and he surrendered, then it appeared that it was someone else, he has the pre-emption' because people differ in character; some desire his company, and some avoid him for fear of his evil.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics. First, if it becomes known that the sale was for dinars worth a thousand dirhams, the shafi' loses his right according to Abu Yusuf. This is part of a previous discussion. Next, the text from al-Muhit addresses the case where the shafi' surrenders his right, and later the parties admit that the sale was a talji'a (a fictitious sale to circumvent pre-emption). The surrender is valid because the shafi' had surrendered his right based on apparent facts, and after surrender he has no standing to challenge the contract. However, if the talji'a is proven before the shafi' receives the property, his right may revive. The text then discusses gift transactions that turn out to be sales, and the effect of giving an option. There is a disagreement between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether the shafi' gets his right back if the buyer gives the seller an option and the sale is rescinded. Finally, the author returns to the rule that if the shafi' is told the buyer is a specific person and surrenders, but later learns the buyer is someone else, he retains his right because personal characteristics matter.

Key Terms
التلجئة (al-talji'a): A fictitious sale, often used to deprive the pre-emptor of his right by pretending to sell, but actually intending to keep the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a shafi' unconditionally surrenders his right of pre-emption, and later the buyer and seller admit the sale was a talji'a (fictitious), what happens?
A) The shafi' gets his right back automatically.
B) The shafi' may sue to invalidate the surrender.
C) The shafi' does not get his right back because he had already surrendered.
D) The surrender is void ab initio because the sale was invalid.

Key Takeaway
Surrender of shuf'a is binding even if the underlying sale is later shown to be a talji'a; the right is lost permanently except in cases of mistaken identity or certain gift transactions.

Effect of Price/Commodity Discrepancy on Shuf'a Surrender
Expansion on shuf'a surrender validity under misrepresentation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a shafi's surrender of shuf'a when the reported price or commodity differs from the actual facts, distinguishing between detriment and benefit to the shafi'.

Core Idea
Shuf'a surrender is invalid if the actual terms are as good as or better than reported; valid only if worse.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on scenarios where a shafi' (holder of pre-emption right) surrenders his right based on incomplete or inaccurate information. The rulings demonstrate a consistent principle: the validity of the surrender depends on whether the actual price or item is more or less favorable than reported. Understanding this protects the shafi' from being misled and ensures fairness in property transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reported vs actual facts
In each scenario, first determine what the shafi' was told (price or commodity) and what turned out to be true. For example, told price is a slave, actual is a slave-girl.
The key is to compare reported and actual, not to assume one is correct.
2
Assess whether the actual is better or worse
Compare the value of the actual item to the reported one, or the actual price to the reported price. If the actual is of equal or greater value (for the shafi' receiving the property) or lower price (for the shafi' paying), it is better.
Better means the shafi' would be in a more advantageous position.
3
Apply the rule: better -> surrender invalid, worse -> surrender valid
If the actual terms are as good as or better than reported, the surrender is invalid and the shafi' retains his right. If the actual terms are worse, the surrender is valid and the shafi' loses his right.
This is the core principle illustrated by the examples.
4
Consider exceptional cases and intra-madhhab disputes
Note the difference between Zufar/Abu Hanifa who hold surrender always invalid if the item type differs, and al-Karkhi/others who consider value comparison. Also note the half/whole scenarios where the analysis uses the defect of partnership.
These enrich the application of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : ولو بلغه أن الثمن عبد فظهر أنه جارية ينظر إن كان قيمة الجارية كقيمة العبد أو أكثر بطلت وإن كان أقل من قيمة العبد لا تبطل فهو كما لو أخبر بالثمن ألف وظهر أقل. ولو أخبر أن الثمن ألف درهم فسلم فإذا هو مائة دينار لم يذكره في الأصل أيضاً. وذكر الكرخي ينظر؛ إن كان قيمة الدنانير ألف درهم أو أكثر صح التسليم وهو قول شيخ الإسلام؛ كذا في التجريد. وروي عن زفر له في الوجهين الشفعة وهو قول الإمام. ولو أخبر أنه باع نصفها فسلم ثم علم أنه باع كلها فله الشفعة لأن من رغب عن البعض لعيب الشركة لا يكون راغباً عن الكل وليس فيه عيب ولو أخبر أنه باع الكل فسلم ثم علم أنه باع نصفها بطلت شفعته لأن من رغب عنها وليس بها عيب الشركة كان راغباً عنها وبها عيب الشركة بالطريق الأولى. قالوا وتأويلها أن يكون ثمن النصف ثمن الكل فلو أخبر أنه باع الكل بألف ثم علم أنه باع النصف بخمسمائة فإنه يجب أن يكون على شفعته لأنه إذا رغب في الأول لعجزه عن الألف فلا يكون راغباً عن الخمسمائة ولو أخبر أنها بيعت بألف فسلم الشفيع الشفعة ثم حط البائع عن المشتري شيئاً من الثمن وقبل الحط فله الشفعة لأنه يلتحق بأصل العقد فصار كما لو أخبر أنها بيعت بألف فظهر أنها بيعت بأقل . منه، ولو زاد البائع مشتري الدار عليها عبداً أو أمة بعد ما سلم الشفيع الشفعة كان للشفيع أن يأخذ الدار بحصتها من الثمن لأنه تبين أن حصة الدار من الثمن أقل، ولو قضى القاضي له بالشفعة ولم يعلم بالثمن ثم علم فله الخيار لأن رضاه بالأخذ إنما يتم إذا علم بالثمن ا هـ . وفي التجريد وغيره أخبر أن الثمن عبد أو جارية فظهر أنه مكيل أو موزون فهو على شفعته ا هـ .
And in al-Muhit: If he is informed that the price is a slave, then it appears it is a slave-girl: if the value of the slave-girl is equal to the value of the slave or more, the shuf'a is invalidated; if it is less than the value of the slave, it is not invalidated. This is like if he was informed that the price is one thousand and it appears less. And if he was informed that the price is one thousand dirhams and he surrendered, then it turns out to be one hundred dinars—he did not mention it in the original text either. Al-Karkhi mentioned: consideration is given; if the value of the dinars is one thousand dirhams or more, the surrender is valid, and this is the statement of Shaykh al-Islam; so in al-Tajrid. And it is narrated from Zufar: he has shuf'a in both cases, and it is the statement of the Imam. And if he was informed that he sold half of it and he surrendered, then he learns that he sold all of it, he has shuf'a, because one who refrains from part due to the defect of partnership does not refrain from the whole, and there is no defect in it. And if he was informed that he sold the whole and he surrendered, then he learns that he sold half of it, his shuf'a is invalidated, because one who refrained from it while it had no defect of partnership was refraining from it, and the defect of partnership exists in it by primary reasoning. They said: its interpretation is that the price of the half is the price of the whole. For if he was informed that he sold the whole for one thousand and then he learns that he sold the half for five hundred, then he should have his shuf'a, because if he refrained from the first due to inability to pay one thousand, he is not refraining from the five hundred. And if he was informed that it was sold for one thousand, and the shafi' surrendered his shuf'a, then the seller reduced something from the price for the buyer and he accepted the reduction, then he has shuf'a, because it attaches to the original contract, so it becomes as if he was informed that it was sold for one thousand and it appears it was sold for less. From it: And if the seller of the house added a slave or slave-girl to it after the shafi' surrendered his shuf'a, then the shafi' may take the house with its share of the price, because it becomes clear that the share of the house from the price is less. And if the judge gave him shuf'a without him knowing the price, then he comes to know it, he has the option, because his consent to taking is only complete when he knows the price. End quote. And in al-Tajrid and others: if he is informed that the price is a slave or slave-girl, then it appears it is something measured or weighed, he retains his shuf'a. End quote.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This is an expansion from the commentator (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) on various scenarios where the reported price or item sold differs from the actual facts, affecting the validity of the shafi's surrender of shuf'a. The passage begins with a case from al-Muhit: if the shafi' is told the price is a slave but it turns out to be a slave-girl, we look at the value. If the slave-girl's value equals or exceeds the slave's, the surrender is invalid because the shafi' was mistaken about the value; if less, the surrender stands because the actual price is lower, which the shafi' would prefer. Similarly, if told the price is 1000 dirhams but it is 100 dinars, al-Karkhi says to compare the current value of the dinars to 1000 dirhams. If equal or more, surrender valid because no loss; if less, surrender invalid. Zufar and Abu Hanifa (Imam) hold that shuf'a remains in both cases, i.e., surrender is ineffective regardless of value. Next, if the shafi' is told half the property was sold but it was actually all sold, surrender is invalid because he refrained from half due to the defect of partnership (shuyu'), but the whole has no such defect, so his surrender does not apply. Conversely, if told all was sold but only half was sold, surrender is valid because he refrained from the whole (which had no defect), so he would have refrained from the half with the same reasoning (since the defect of partnership is present in the half a fortiori). A key point: if the price of the half equals the price of the whole, the analysis changes. If he surrendered due to inability to pay the reported high price (e.g., 1000 for the whole), and then learns the actual price for the half is only 500, his surrender is invalid because his inability was only for the higher amount. Also, if after surrender the seller reduces the price for the buyer, the shafi' may still claim shuf'a because the reduction relates back to the contract. Similarly, if the seller adds a slave to the sale after surrender, the shafi' may take the house at its reduced share of the price. Finally, if the judge awards shuf'a without the shafi' knowing the price, he has the option to rescind after learning it. The Tajrid adds that if the reported item (slave/slave-girl) turns out to be a measured/weighted commodity, shuf'a remains because the category is different but the value may be comparable. All these rulings illustrate the Hanafi principle that shuf'a is built on compensation and the shafi's consent is tied to accurate information.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): The right of pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property by compensating the buyer.
التسليم (al-taslīm): The act of the shafi' surrendering or relinquishing his right of shuf'a.
الثمن (al-thaman): The price paid for the property in the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A shafi' is told that the property was sold for 1000, and he surrenders. Later it turns out the actual price was 800. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The surrender is valid; he loses shuf'a.
B) The surrender is invalid; he retains shuf'a.
C) He has the option to take the property at the lower price.
D) The surrender is valid only if the buyer agrees.

Key Takeaway
A shafi's surrender of shuf'a is valid only when the actual price or commodity is worse; otherwise, the surrender is invalid and the right remains.

Shuf'a: Price in Dinars, Talji'a, and the Finality of Surrender
Rulings on shuf'a: price in dinars, talji'a after surrender, gift/sale distinction, and option dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Abu Yusuf opinion on shuf'a when the price is in dinars, explain why admitting talji'a after surrender does not revive shuf'a, and compare the two Hanafi narrations regarding the effect of a one-day option.

Core Idea
Surrender of shuf'a is final—later collusion or option exercise does not revive it; only surrender based on misrepresentation may be revisited.

This lesson examines two nuanced scenarios where the shafi's right appears to be affected by subsequent events. First, the ruling when the price is expressed in dinars of equivalent value. Then, the effect of a collusive sale (talji'a) being admitted after the shafi' has surrendered. The text also presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the buyer granting a one-day option to cancel. Understanding these nuances highlights the principle that once shuf'a is voluntarily surrendered, it is generally not revived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
The author states that if the property was sold for dinars worth 1000 dirhams, there is no shuf'a. Note that this is attributed to Abu Yusuf. Understand that the currency of the price can affect the shuf'a right.
This is a specific condition that negates shuf'a; the general rule requires a valid sale with a stated price.
2
Analyze the talji'a scenario
The text from al-Muhit presents: the shafi' surrenders, then the buyer admits the sale was collusive (talji'a). The ruling states that shuf'a does not revive because after surrender the shafi' has no remaining right. Even if collusion is proven by clear evidence, the right does not return.
Compare to the case before surrender: if collusion is discovered before the shafi' surrenders, he can still claim shuf'a.
3
Distinguish gift with compensation vs. true gift
If the shafi' surrendered thinking the transaction was a gift for compensation (i.e., a sale), and it turns out it was a sale, shuf'a does not return. But if he surrendered in a gift without any compensation and later both parties confirm it was a gift with compensation, shuf'a returns.
The key is whether the shafi' was aware of the true nature; a mistaken surrender in a pure gift case revives the right.
4
Examine the option dispute from al-Nawadir
After the shafi' surrenders, the buyer gives the seller a one-day option. If the seller cancels, does shuf'a revive? According to Muhammad (via Ibn Sama'a), it does not; according to Abu Yusuf, it does. Understand the thamarah (practical difference).
The mufta bihi is likely Muhammad's view (finality of surrender), but both are valid riwayat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو بان أنها بيعت بدنانير قيمتها ألف فلا شفعة (له وهو قول أبي يوسف. وقد بينا المسألة بفروعها فيما تقدم. وفي المحيط : سلم الشفيع الشفعة فقال المشتري للبائع كان تلجئة لا يتجدد شفعته لأنه بعد ما سلم لم يبق له حق فصح إقرارهما بأن البيع تلجئة فكان فاسداً، ولو ثبت معاينة أن البيع تلجئة لا يتجدد للشفيع حق الشفعة بخلاف ما لو كان قبل التسلم لأن حق الشفيع ثبت من حيث الظاهر فإقرارهما يتضمن إبطال حقه فلا يقبل تسلم الشفيع في هبة بعوض فظهر أنه بيع لم تعد الشفعة، ولو سلم في هبة بغير شرط العوض ثم تصادقا أنه كان بشرط العوض فله الشفعة وفي النوادر ولو سلم الشفعة ثم جعل المشتري للبائع خيار يوم جاز فإن نقض البائع البيع في ذلك اليوم لا يتجدد للشفيع حق الشفعة؛ رواه ابن سماعة عن محمد، وروى ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف أن له الشفعة ا هـ .
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if it becomes clear that it was sold for dinars the value of which is one thousand, there is no shuf'a for him, and it is the statement of Abu Yusuf. And we have already explained the issue with its branches earlier. And in al-Muhit: The shafi' surrendered his shuf'a, then the buyer said to the seller, 'It was a collusive sale (talji'a),' his shuf'a does not renew, because after he surrendered, he has no right left, so their acknowledgment that the sale was talji'a is valid, so it is null. And if it is established by visual evidence that the sale was talji'a, the shafi's right of shuf'a does not renew, unlike if it was before surrender, because the shafi's right was established apparently, so their acknowledgment entails revocation of his right, so it is not accepted. And if the shafi' surrendered in a gift for compensation, then it appears it was a sale, his shuf'a does not return. And if he surrendered in a gift without a condition of compensation, then they both testify that it was with a condition of compensation, he has shuf'a. And in al-Nawadir: And if he surrendered his shuf'a, then the buyer gave the seller a one-day option, it is permissible; if the seller cancels the sale on that day, the shafi's right of shuf'a does not renew; narrated by Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad. And Ibn Sama'a narrated from Abu Yusuf that he has shuf'a. End quote.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage begins with a direct ruling from the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq): if the property was sold for dinars worth 1000 dirhams, the shafi' has no shuf'a according to Abu Yusuf. The commentator notes that this issue was already covered earlier with its branches. Then it quotes from al-Muhit a discussion about talji'a (a collusive sale meant to deprive the shafi'): if the shafi' has already surrendered his shuf'a, and later the buyer and seller admit that the sale was collusive, the shuf'a does not revive. The reason is that after surrender, the shafi' has no remaining right; therefore, their admission (which would normally invalidate the sale) does not benefit him. Even if the collusion is proven by clear evidence, the right does not revive, as opposed to a situation where the shafi' has not yet taken possession (tasallum) and the shuf'a right is still intact. The text then distinguishes between cases where the shafi' surrendered mistakenly thinking it was a gift (with compensation) versus a true gift: if the shafi' surrendered in a gift with compensation (i.e., a sale disguised as a gift), then the actual nature becomes known, his shuf'a does not return because he surrendered based on a different transaction. However, if he surrendered in a gift without any condition of compensation, and later both parties confirm that it was actually a gift with compensation, the shafi' gets shuf'a. Finally, al-Nawadir reports two narrations: according to Muhammad (via Ibn Sama'a), if the shafi' surrenders and then the buyer gives the seller a one-day option to cancel, and the seller cancels, the shuf'a does not revive; but according to Abu Yusuf, it does revive. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
التلجئة (al-talji'a): A collusive sale where the seller and buyer pretend to sell but actually intend to deprive the shafi' of his right; the sale is legally invalid.
الخيار (al-khiyār): The option to rescind a contract; in this context, a one-day option given by the buyer to the seller.
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): The pre-emption right of a co-owner or neighbor to buy a property sold to a third party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text from al-Muhit, if a shafi' surrenders his shuf'a and later the buyer and seller admit the sale was talji'a, what is the ruling?
A) The shuf'a is automatically revived.
B) The shuf'a does not revive because the shafi' no longer has a right.
C) The shuf'a revives only if the shafi' had not yet taken possession.
D) The shuf'a revives only if the admission is made in court.

Key Takeaway
Surrender of shuf'a extinguishes the right permanently; only a surrender based on misrepresentation about the nature of the transaction may allow revival.

Shuf'a Survives When Buyer's Identity Is Mistaken
States that if shafi' surrenders based on wrong identity, he retains shuf'a, with rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a shafi' retains shuf'a if he surrenders based on the wrong buyer's identity, and explain the rational proof behind it.

Core Idea
Surrender of shuf'a is buyer-specific; a mistaken party does not forfeit the right.

In preemption law, the identity of the buyer matters because people's characters differ. This lesson examines a scenario where the shafi' is misinformed and surrenders based on that misinformation. The Hanafi school holds that the surrender is ineffective, preserving the shafi' right.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
The shafi' is told the buyer is a specific person (Zayd) and surrenders his right of shuf'a. Later, it turns out the actual buyer is someone else (Amr).
2
Identify the ruling
The shafi' retains his right of shuf'a. The surrender based on false information does not count.
This is the explicit ruling in the matn.
3
Understand the rationale
People differ in character. A person may be willing to be a neighbour to one but not another. Surrender is specific to the known buyer.
This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) based on social differences.
4
Apply to multiple buyers
If the shafi' knows the buyer is one of two, he can take the share of the unknown buyer because his surrender did not apply to that share.
This extends the logic.
5
Summarize the legal principle
The validity of surrender depends on correct identification of the buyer. Mistaken identity does not nullify shuf'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن قيل له أن المشتري فلان فسلم ثم ظهر أنه غيره فله الشفعة) لتفاوت الناس في الأخلاق فمنهم من يرغب في معاشرته، ومنهم من يجتنب مخافة شره هذا القدر فالتسليم في حق البعض لا يكون تسليماً في حق غيره، ولو علم أن المشتري هو مع غيره كان له أن يأخذ نصيب غيره لأن التسليم لم يوجد في حقه. قال محمد في الجامع الصغير : ولو قال الشفيع سلمت الشفعة في هذه الدار إن كنت اشتريتها لنفسك وقد اشتراها لغيره فهذا ليس بتسليم وذلك لأن الشفيع علق التسليم بشرط، هذا التعليق لأن تسليم وصح الشفعة إسقاط الحق كالطلاق فصح تعليقه بالشرط ولا يترك إلا بعد وجوده. قال صاحب العناية بعد ما نقل كلام محمد :هذا وهذا كما ترى يناقض قوله ولا يتعلق إسقاطه بالشرط الجائز فبالفاسد أولى ا هـ . وقد يجاب بأنه فرق بين شرط و شرط فما سبق كان من الشروط التي تدل على الإعراض عن الشفعة والرضا بالجوار مطلقاً، وما ذكر هنا من الشروط التي لا تدل على الإعراض ولا على الرضا فتأمل .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he is told that the buyer is so-and-so, and he surrenders, then it appears it is someone else, he has shuf'a) because people differ in character; among them is one who desires his company, and among them is one who avoids him out of fear of his evil. This much: So surrender with respect to some is not surrender with respect to others. And if he knew that the buyer is together with someone else, he may take the share of the other, because surrender did not apply to him. Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And if the shafi' says, 'I surrender shuf'a in this house if you bought it for yourself,' but he bought it for someone else, this is not surrender, because the shafi' conditioned the surrender on a condition. This conditioning is because surrender of shuf'a is a relinquishment of a right like divorce, so it can be conditioned by a condition, and it is not abandoned except after its fulfillment. The author of al-'Inayah said after quoting Muhammad: 'This and this, as you see, contradicts his statement that its relinquishment is not attached to a valid condition, so to an invalid one a fortiori.' End quote. And it may be answered that there is a difference between conditions: what preceded were conditions that indicate disinterest in shuf'a and absolute satisfaction with the neighborhood, whereas what is mentioned here are conditions that do not indicate disinterest nor satisfaction, so ponder.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues. First, the matn ruling: if the shafi' is told the buyer is a specific person and he surrenders based on that, but then it appears the buyer is someone else, he keeps his shuf'a. The reason is people's characters differ—one might be willing to live beside one person but not another. Surrender is specific to the known buyer; it does not apply to a different person. Similarly, if the shafi' learns that the buyer is actually more than one, he may take the share of the unknown buyer because his surrender was only for the known one. Second, Muhammad al-Shaybani discusses a conditional surrender: if the shafi' says, 'I surrender shuf'a if you bought it for yourself,' but the buyer bought it for someone else, this is not a valid surrender because the condition was not met. The analogy with divorce (talaq) is used: both are relinquishments of rights and can be conditioned. However, the commentator from al-'Inayah points out a contradiction: elsewhere it is stated that relinquishment of shuf'a cannot be attached to a condition (i.e., a conditional surrender is invalid). The reply distinguishes between conditions that show an absolute disinterest in the property (like saying 'I have no desire' with a condition) and conditions that merely suspend the surrender on a specific scenario. The latter are valid because they do not indicate a definitive waiver. This is a subtle point of Hanafi jurisprudence on the nature of rights and conditions.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): The right of preemption in property sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, if the shafi' surrenders based on being told the buyer is Zayd, but the buyer is actually Amr, what is the ruling?
A) The surrender is valid because the shafi' voluntarily gave up his right.
B) The surrender is invalid and shuf'a remains.
C) The surrender is valid only if Amr is of similar character to Zayd.
D) The surrender is invalid only if the shafi' can prove he was misled.

Key Takeaway
Surrender of shuf'a is person-specific; mistaken identity preserves the right.

Conditional Surrender of Shuf'a: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discusses validity of conditional surrender and the intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions indicating disinterest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view on conditional surrender of shuf'a and distinguish between conditions that render the surrender absolute and those that do not.

Core Idea
A conditional surrender is valid if the condition does not indicate permanent disinterest.

Can a shafi' condition his surrender? Muhammad al-Shaybani says yes, by analogy to divorce. But a commentator from al-'Inayah points out a contradiction: elsewhere it says a conditional waiver is invalid. The resolution lies in the type of condition: conditions showing disinterest make the surrender absolute, while others keep it contingent.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario from al-Jami' al-Saghir
The shafi' says: 'I surrender shuf'a in this house if you bought it for yourself.' The buyer bought it for someone else.
2
Identify Muhammad's ruling
Muhammad says this is not a valid surrender because the condition was not met. The shafi' retains his right.
The condition prevents the surrender from taking effect.
3
Understand the analogy
Surrender of shuf'a is like divorce: both are relinquishments of rights (isqat haqq) and can be conditioned.
This is a qiyas to talaq.
4
Recognize the objection
The author of al-'Inayah notes that elsewhere it is stated that a conditional relinquishment is invalid. So this seems contradictory.
The contradiction is apparent, not real.
5
Learn the resolution
The difference is that conditions implying disinterest (e.g., 'I have no need') make the surrender absolute, while conditions like 'if you bought for yourself' do not indicate disinterest.
Conditions that show 'i'rad' (turning away) render surrender irrevocable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
