Types of Division and the Application of Options in Co-Owned Property
Classifies division types and explains the application of options (khiyarat) to each type, with an intra-Hanafi difference on option of sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the three types of division according to the Hanafi school and determine which options (khiyarat) apply to each type.

Core Idea
Division is classified by genus and fungibility; the applicability of options depends on this classification.

In this lesson, we explore the commentary from al-Fatawa al-Sughra, which divides division into three categories and maps the three options (khiyar al-shart, al-ru'yah, al-'ayb) onto them. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying the legal consequences to each division scenario. We also note an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the option of sight in non-fungible property of one type.

Guided Path
1
List the three types of division
Identify from the commentary: (1) Division not forced – different genera; (2) Division forced in fungibles (mithliyyat) like weighed/measured goods; (3) Division forced in non-fungibles of one type (e.g., clothes, cows, sheep).
The classification is based on the nature of the property.
2
Identify the three options (khiyarat)
The options are: khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation), khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight), and khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect). Note that these options arise from the transaction of division.
Division is considered a type of exchange (mu'awada).
3
Map options to division types
In division of different genera, all three options apply. In forced division of fungibles, only khiyar al-'ayb applies (not khiyar al-shart or al-ru'yah). In forced division of non-fungibles of one type, khiyar al-'ayb applies, and according to the sound view, also khiyar al-ru'yah.
The mapping is based on the nature of the property: in fungibles, sight is unnecessary because items are identical by description; stipulation is excluded because division is immediate.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi difference
Regarding non-fungibles of one type, there is a narration from Abu Sulayman that khiyar al-ru'yah is established. This is considered the correct view and the basis for fatwa. The other view (not explicit) would exclude it.
The text says 'upon it is the fatwa' (عليه الفتوى), indicating the operative position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ويجبر في متحد الجنس عند طلب أحد الشركاء لا في غيره) يعني إذا طلب بعض الشركاء القسمة يجبر الآبي على القسمة في متحد الجنس، سواء كان من ذوات الأمثال أو لا، ولا يجبر في غير متحد الجنس كالغنم مع الإبل لما بينا من المعنى. وفي غاية البيان قال في الفتاوى الصغرى القسمة ثلاثة أنواع : قسمة لا يجبر الآبي عليها كقسمة الأجناس المختلفة، وقسمة يجبر عليها الآبي كقسمة ذوات الأمثال كالمكيل والموزون، وقسمة يجبر الآبي في غير المثليات كالثياب من نوع واحد والبقر والغنم. والخيارات ثلاثة: خيار شرط، وخيار رؤية وخيار عيب. ففي قسمة الأجناس المختلفة تثبت الخيارات الثلاث، وفي قسمة ذوات الأمثال كالمكيل يثبت خيار العيب دون خيار الشرط والرؤية، فخيار الرؤية والعيب يثبتان من غر شرط بخلاف خيار الشرط. وفي قسمة الثياب من نوع واحد والبقر والغنم يثبت خيار العيب وهل يثبت خيار الرؤية؟ على رواية أبي سليمان يثبت وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى ويثبت فيه خيار العيب من غير خلاف ا هـ . وفي الذخيرة : القاضي لا يقسم الأجناس المختلفة قسمة إذا أبى بعض الشركاء بأن كان بينهم إبل وغنم وطلب جمع أحدهم من القاضي أن يجمع نصيبه في الإبل والبقر والغنم فالقاضي لا يقسم على هذا الوجه، وفي الجنس المتحد يقسم قسمة جمع عند طلب البعض بأن كان بينهم غنم كثيرة أو إبل كثيرة وطلب أحدهم من القاضي أن يجمع نصيبه في طائفة منها فعل القاضي ذلك ا هـ . وفي النهاية : اعترض على قوله يجبر بأن المبادلة معتبرة فيها فكيف يجبر؟ وأجيب بأنه يجبر لدفع الضرر عن غيره كالغريم يحبس حتى يباع ماله لبعض الدين ولهذا لا يثبت حكم الغرور فيها حتى لو أخذ أحدهما الدار وبنى في نصيبه فاستحق الدار التي بنى فيها لا يرجع على صاحبه بقيمة بنائه إذا نقض ا هـ . وظاهر العبارة صادق بطلب صاحب القليل والكثير وسيأتي تقييده.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And he is compelled in the homogenous genus upon the request of one of the partners, not in other than it) meaning: if some of the partners request division, the refusing partner is compelled to division in homogenous genus, whether it is of the fungible type or not; he is not compelled in non-homogenous genus like sheep with camels, for the meaning we have explained. The commentary then elaborates by quoting al-Fatawa al-Sughra, which classifies division into three types: (1) division not forced (different genera), (2) division forced in fungibles, (3) division forced in non-fungibles of one type. It also explains how the three options (خيارات) apply: in different genera, all three options exist; in fungibles, only the option of defect; in non-fungibles of one type, both option of defect and, according to the sound position, option of sight apply. The text then cites al-Dhakhirah on how a judge handles requests for collective division (قسمة جمع) in homogeneous herds. Finally, it addresses an objection from al-Nihayah: if division involves exchange, how can one be compelled? The answer is that compulsion is for harm prevention, analogous to imprisoning a debtor to sell his property, and therefore the effect of deceit (غرور) does not apply—meaning if one partner builds on his share and it turns out the property was not fully owned, he cannot claim compensation from the other.

Key Terms
متحد الجنس (muttaḥid al-jins): Property that belongs to the same genus, e.g., sheep with sheep, gold with gold; forced division applies.
جبر (jabr): Legal compulsion upon a renuant co-owner to accept division when one partner requests it in homogeneous property.
خيار (khiyār): The right to cancel or confirm a transaction upon discovering a defect, after sight, or as per stipulation; applied here to division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the option of sight in division of fungibles (mithliyyat) such as wheat?
A) It is established without dispute
B) It is established only by stipulation
C) It is not established
D) It is established only in non-fungibles of one type

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of division determines which options apply; the option of defect always applies, while the option of sight is established in non-fungibles of one type according to the sound view.

Appointing a Divider: Salary and Qualifications
Rulings on appointing a divider, his salary, and required qualifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options for the divider's salary, explain why fee is per capita under Abu Hanifa, and list the three required qualifications of a divider.

Core Idea
A divider's salary is best from the public treasury, but if not, the fee is split equally per capita, not by share size.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the appointment of a property divider (qāsim) and his compensation. The matn presents two scenarios: a recommended arrangement from the treasury, and a fallback fee paid by the co-owners. The commentary clarifies the legal nature of division and the required qualifications of the divider.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two salary options
First, note that the matn gives two scenarios: (1) recommended appointment with salary from the public treasury (bayt al-māl), and (2) if not possible, appointment with a fee paid by the co-owners. Distinguish the legal category: the first is mandub (recommended), the second is permissible.
The salary from treasury is considered akin to a judge's salary.
2
Understand the legal analogy
The commentary explains that division (qismah) resembles judgment (qaḍāʾ) because it ends disputes, so the divider's salary from treasury is justified. However, division is not truly judgment; the judge is not obliged to perform it personally, only to compel the reluctant co-owner to divide. Therefore, taking a fee for division is permissible, unlike for judgment.
This distinction allows the judge to charge for division but not for judging.
3
Analyze the fee distribution
When the fee is paid by the co-owners, the matn says 'after the heads' (baʿd al-ruʾūs), meaning equally per capita, not proportionally to shares. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentary adds that the judge estimates a market-rate fee to prevent abuse, and the best option is still payment from treasury to avoid suspicion.
Per capita means each co-owner pays the same amount, regardless of their share size.
4
List the qualifications and the scholarly discussion
The divider must be just (ʿadl), trustworthy (amīn), and knowledgeable (ʿālim) in division. The commentary, via Taj al-Shariʿah, discusses why trustworthiness is mentioned separately: justice implies apparent trustworthiness, but actual reliability may be absent, so explicit mention is necessary. The passage ends with a rebuttal, but the principle remains.
These three qualities mirror those required for a judge, reinforcing the analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وندب نصب قاسم رزقه في بيت المال ليقسم بلا أجر) يعني يستحب نصب قاسم ورزقه في بيت المال لأن القسمة من جنس القضاء من حيث إنه يتم به قطع المنازعة فأشبه رزق القاضي، ولأن منفعته تعود إلى العامة كمنفعة القضاء والمقاتل والمفتي فتكون كفايته في بيت المال لأنه أعد لمصالحهم كمنفعة هؤلاء. وفي العتابية وغيرها : وينصب قاسماً ويجوز للقاضي أن يقسم بنفسه ويأخذ على ذلك من المتقاسمين أجرة، وهذا القاضي لأن القسمة ليست بقضاء على الحقيقة حتى لا يفترض على القاضي مباشرتها وإنما الذي يفترض عليه جبر الآبي على القسمة إلا أن لها شبهاً بالقضاء لأنها تستفاد منه ا هـ. قال رحمه الله : (وإلا نصب قاسماً يقسم بأجرة بعد الرؤوس) يعني إن لم ينصب قاسماً رزقه في بيت المال نصبه وجعل رزقه على المتقاسمين لأن النفع لهم على الخصوص وليس بقضاء حقيقة حتى جاز للقاضي أن يأخذ الأجرة على القسمة وإن كان لا يجوز له على القضاء إلا : أنه لا يفترض عليه أن يقسم عليهم بالمباشرة ومباشرة القضاء فرض عليه ويقدر له القاضي أجرة مثله كي لا يطمع في أموالهم ويتحكم بالزيادة، والأفضل أن رزقه من بيت المال لأنه أرفع من التهمة. وقوله بعدد الرؤوس يعني يجب عليهم الأجرة على عدد الرؤوس ولا يتفاوت بتفاوت الأنصباء، وهذا عند الإمام كما سيجيء بيانه عن قريب. قال (ويجب أن يكون عدلاً أميناً عالماً بالقسمة لأنه من جنس عمل القضاء لأنه لا بد من الاعتماد على قوله والقدرة على القسمة وذلك بما ذكرنا . قال تاج الشريعة ذكر الأمانة بعد العدالة وإن كانت من لوازمه الجواز أن يكون غير ظاهر الأمانة ورد بهذا ما به يلزم من ظهور العدالة ظهور الأمانة، ورد عليه بأن المذكور العدالة لا ظهورها فاستلزم ظهورها ظهور الأمانة لا يقتضي استدراك ذكر الإمانة فإن قلت: لا يجوز أن يراد بالعدالة ظهورها كما أريد الأمانة من
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And is recommended the appointment of a divider whose sustenance is in the public treasury to divide without fee) meaning: it is recommended to appoint a divider and his sustenance is from the public treasury because division is akin to judgment in that it brings about the cessation of dispute, so it resembles the sustenance of a judge, and because its benefit returns to the public like the benefit of the judiciary, the fighter, and the mufti, so his maintenance is from the public treasury since it is prepared for their interests like the benefit of these. And in al-Atabiyyah and others: A divider is appointed, and it is permissible for the judge to divide by himself and take a fee from those dividing, and this judge because division is not truly judgment such that direct performance is not obligatory upon the judge; rather what is obligatory upon him is to compel the renuant to division, except that it resembles judgment because it is derived from it, end quote. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And otherwise he appoints a divider who divides for a fee according to heads) meaning: if he does not appoint a divider whose sustenance is from the public treasury, he appoints one and makes his sustenance upon the co-dividers because the benefit is specifically for them and it is not truly judgment, so it is permissible for the judge to take a fee for division even though he is not permitted to do so for judgment, except that it is not obligatory upon him to divide for them directly, while direct judgment is obligatory upon him. And the judge estimates his fee at the like [of the market] so that he does not covet their wealth and arbitrarily increase. And the best is that his sustenance be from the public treasury because it is more removed from suspicion. And his saying 'according to heads' means the fee is obligatory upon them according to the number of heads and does not vary according to the disparity of shares, and this is according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] as will be explained shortly. He said: (And he must be just, trustworthy, knowledgeable of division) because it is akin to the work of judgment, because reliance must be placed on his word and the ability to divide, and that is as we have mentioned. Taj al-Shari'ah said: He mentioned trustworthiness after justice even though it is among its necessities, [and the necessity] is that he be not apparently trustworthy. And this is refuted by what necessitates from the appearance of justice the appearance of trustworthiness. It was countered that what is mentioned is justice, not its appearance, so the entailment of appearance of justice to appearance of trustworthiness does not justify the addition of mentioning trustworthiness. For if you say: It is not permissible that by justice is meant its appearance, just as trustworthiness is intended from [the statement].
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage covers the rulings on the appointment of a divider (qasim) for shared property. The matn states two options: (1) it is recommended (mandub) to appoint a divider whose salary is from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) so he divides without charging the parties; (2) if that is not done, a divider is appointed who charges a fee to be divided equally among the co-owners per capita (not proportional to shares). The commentary explains that division resembles judgment (qada) in ending disputes, so the divider's salary from the treasury is analogous to a judge's salary. However, division is not truly judgment—the judge is not obliged to personally perform it; he only must compel a renuant partner—so it is acceptable for the judge to take a fee for division, unlike judgment. The fee is set at the market rate to prevent abuse. The best option is payment from the treasury to avoid suspicion. The passage then states the required qualifications: the divider must be just (ʿadl), trustworthy (amin), and knowledgeable in division (ʿalim bi al-qismah). Taj al-Shariʿah discusses why trustworthiness is mentioned separately from justice: justice implies apparent righteousness, but trustworthiness is needed for actual reliability. The text ends with a counter-argument that justice as mentioned does not necessarily imply its appearance, so the addition is still valid. The discussion is cut off at the end of the page.

Key Terms
قاسم (qāsim): A person appointed to divide jointly owned property among co-owners, with qualifications of justice, trustworthiness, and knowledge.
بيت المال (bayt al-māl): The public treasury of the Muslim state, from which it is recommended to pay the divider's salary.
أجرة بعد الرؤوس (ujrah baʿd al-ruʾūs): A fee for division that is divided equally per capita among the co-owners, not according to their shares.
عدل أمين عالم (ʿadl amīn ʿālim): The three required qualities of a divider: just (righteous in religious observance), trustworthy (reliable in handling property), and knowledgeable (knowing the rules of division).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Equally per capita (after the heads)
C) According to the number of disputes
D) It is paid solely by the one requesting division

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends the divider's salary from the public treasury, but if not, the fee is shared equally per capita among co-owners, and the divider must be just, trustworthy, and knowledgeable.

Appointing a Qasim: Fee by Heads and Required Qualifications
Ruling on appointment, fee basis, and qasim qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a qasim, explain the basis for fee distribution by heads, and identify the qualifications required of the qasim.

Core Idea
Fee equality by heads reflects uniform work; qasim must combine justice, trustworthiness, and knowledge.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the judge's role in appointing a divider (qasim) for joint property. It clarifies that if no treasury-funded qasim is available, the judge must appoint one and the fee is shared equally among partners—a key intra-Hanafi dispute. The passage also lays out the essential qualifications of the qasim, emphasizing that even apparent justice does not guarantee trustworthiness, hence the explicit mention of both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what the act is (appointing a qasim) and its legal status (obligatory on the judge when no treasury official exists; fee on partners).
2
State the hukm level
The judge's duty to appoint a qasim with a fee from partners is wajib kifayah; appointing one with treasury salary is sunnah.
The obligation arises only when partners cannot agree or when a division is needed.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds the fee is divided by number of heads (individual partners); Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) say by share values.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Analyse the proofs
Abu Hanifa: the qasim's work (tamyiz) is uniform, so fee is equal. Sahibayn: fee is a burden of ownership, so proportional to benefit.
The Hanafi response: difficulty in calculating by shares, especially with fractions.
5
Identify the qualifications
The qasim must be just (ʿadala), trustworthy (amana), and knowledgeable (ʿilm) in division. Trustworthiness is mentioned separately because justice alone may not ensure apparent trustworthiness.
Taj al-Shariʽah clarifies this nuance.

Book of Division. Otherwise, he appoints a divider who divides for a fee after the heads. And it is necessary that he be just, trustworthy, knowledgeable in division. In sheep, the option of defect is established. And does the option of sight establish? According to the narration of Abu Sulayman, it establishes, and it is the correct view, and upon it is the fatwa. And the option of defect is established without dispute. End quote. In al-Dhakhirah: The judge does not divide different species if some partners refuse, such as having camels and sheep, and one of them asks the judge to collect his share in camels, cows, and sheep; the judge does not divide in this manner. In the case of a single species, he divides by collection when requested, e.g., many sheep or many camels, and one asks the judge to collect his share in one group; the judge does that. End quote. In al-Nihayah: An objection is raised against his saying "he forces" because exchange is considered here, so how can he force? Answer: He forces to prevent harm to others, like a debtor imprisoned until his property is sold for part of the debt. Hence, the ruling of deception (ghurur) is not established here; if one takes the house and builds in his share, then the house he built in is claimed, he does not recourse to his partner for the value of his building if demolished. End quote. The apparent wording applies to the request of the one with little or much, and its restriction will come. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "And it is recommended to appoint a divider whose sustenance is in the treasury to divide without fee." Meaning, it is recommended to appoint a divider with his sustenance in the treasury because division is akin to judgment in that it ends disputes, so it resembles the sustenance of the judge. And because his benefit returns to the public like the benefit of judgment, fighting, and fatwa, so his sufficiency is in the treasury because it is prepared for their interests like the benefit of these. In al-Atabiyyah and others: He appoints a divider, and it is permissible for the judge to divide himself and take from the partners a fee. This is because division is not truly judgment such that the judge is obligated to perform it; rather, it is only forcing the one who refuses division, but it has a resemblance to judgment because it is derived from it. End quote. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "Otherwise, he appoints a divider who divides for a fee after the heads." Meaning, if he did not appoint a divider whose sustenance is in the treasury, he appoints one and makes his sustenance upon the partners because the benefit is specifically for them, and it is not truly judgment such that the judge is allowed to take a fee for division while he is not allowed for judgment. Rather, he is to divide directly, and direct judgment is obligatory upon him. The judge estimates for him a fee like his equivalent so that he does not covet their wealth and tyrannically increase. And it is better that his sustenance is from the treasury because it is more protective against suspicion. His saying "after the heads" means the fee is incumbent upon them by the number of heads, and it does not vary with the variation of shares. This is according to the Imam as will be explained soon. He said: "And it is necessary that he be just, trustworthy, knowledgeable in division because it is of the type of judgment, for it requires ... and ability in division by what we mentioned." Taj al-Shari'ah said: Mentioning trustworthiness after justice, even if it is among its necessities, its permissibility is that he may not have apparent trustworthiness. This refutes what implies that from the appearance of justice comes the appearance of trustworthiness. It was rebutted that what is mentioned is justice, not its appearance, so its appearance implying the appearance of trustworthiness does not necessitate dispensing with mentioning trustworthiness. If you say: It is not permissible to intend by justice its appearance just as trustworthiness is intended? I said: The appearance of justice from the word 'justice' is not apparent; it is not understood from the word alone without a context. Intending the appearance of trustworthiness from the word 'trustworthiness' occurring in the book initially is apparent justice; there is no need to dispense with mentioning trustworthiness.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by stating the rule: if a qasim (divider) is not appointed with a salary from the public treasury, the judge must appoint one, and the qasim's fee is divided equally among the partners by the number of heads (individuals), not by the value of their shares. The qasim must be just, trustworthy, and knowledgeable in division. The commentary then discusses the related issue of khiyar al-ru'ya (option of sight) in the sale of sheep, citing the correct view. It then cites al-Dhakhirah on how a judge should handle divisions when partners have different types of property. The passage also addresses an objection from al-Nihayah about compulsion in division, answering that it is to prevent harm, like imprisoning a debtor. The main ruling is further explained: it is recommended (sunnah) to appoint a qasim with his salary from the treasury; if not, the judge must appoint one and the partners pay the fee. The fee is by heads per Abu Hanifa, a view that will be detailed later. The commentary then explains why the qasim must be just, trustworthy, and knowledgeable, and includes a discussion by Taj al-Shari'ah on why trustworthiness is mentioned separately even though it is implied by justice—the reason is that the appearance of justice does not necessarily imply apparent trustworthiness, so explicit mention is needed.

Key Terms
قاسم (qāsim): A person appointed by the judge to divide jointly owned property among partners.
قسمة (qisma): The act of dividing joint property; akin to exchange (mubadala) but also has resemblance to judgment.
أجرة (ujra): Fee paid to the qasim for the work of division.
عدالة (ʿadāla): The quality of being just; an explicit condition for the qasim.
أمانة (amāna): Trustworthiness; mentioned separately after 'adala to emphasize that apparent justice does not guarantee trustworthiness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The value of each partner's share
B) The number of partners (heads)

D) The judge's discretion

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the qasim's fee is distributed equally by heads because the work of separation is uniform, and the qasim must be just, trustworthy, and knowledgeable.

Division Without Proof: Movables and Purchased Immovables
Ruling on division without proof for specific property types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dividing inherited movables and purchased immovables without proof of ownership and identify the internal dispute regarding its authority.

Core Idea
In inherited movables and purchased immovables, division is valid by mere claim, due to custom and absence of harm to absent parties.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi ruling that eases the division of jointly owned property when the owners are present and no external claim exists. The key insight is that such division is not a judgment against an absent third party, so formal proof is unnecessary—custom and tacit consent suffice. We will also explore an internal debate about whether this leniency is attributed solely to Imam Abu Hanifa or to the entire school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property types
The passage specifies two categories: inherited movable property (al-manqul al-mawruth) and purchased immovable property (al-aqar al-mushtara). Note that inherited immovables are not included—only purchased ones.
Distinguish: inherited immovables require proof; purchased immovables do not.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator gives two reasons: (1) custom (urf) and meaning (ma'na)—property typically held jointly is presumed to be co-owned; (2) the division is between the claimants themselves, not a judgment against an absent party, so no evidence is needed.
3
Analyze the internal ikhtilaf
Two views exist: (a) this is only Abu Hanifa's position, (b) it is the consensus of the school (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad also). The commentator declares (b) as al-ashah (most correct). However, al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad requires proof, creating a tension.
The phrase 'wa huwa al-ashah' indicates tarjih.
4
Determine the operative ruling
The mufta bihi is the lenient view: division without proof is permissible for inherited movables and purchased immovables. This is based on the tarjih of the later scholars, despite the caution in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
Practical fatwa follows the majority of the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (ويقسم في المنقول والعقار المشتري) يعني يقسم في الموروث المنقول والعقار المشتري وفيما إذا ادعوا الملك ولم يذكروا كيفية انتقاله إليهم قسم بقولهما من غير إقامة بينة، أما في المنقول والعقار المشتري فلما بينا من المعنى والعرف، وأما إذا ادعوا الملك ولم يذكروا كيفية الانتقال إليهم فلأنه ليس القسمة قضاء على الغير فإنهم لم يقروا بالملك لغيرهم ويكون مقتصراً عليهم فيجوز. ثم فيه قيل هذا قول الإمام، وقيل قول الكل وهو الأصح، ولفظ الجامع الصغير يفيد أنه لا يقسم حتى يقيموا البينة على الملك لاحتمال أن يكون الملك في يد غيرهم ا هـ .
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And he divides among movable property and purchased immovable property' meaning he divides inherited movable property and purchased immovable property, and when they claim ownership and do not mention how it transferred to them, it is divided by their statement without establishing evidence. As for movable and purchased immovable, due to what we explained of meaning and custom. As for when they claim ownership and do not mention how it transferred to them, because the division is not a judgment against others, since they have not acknowledged ownership for anyone else and it is confined to them, so it is permissible. Then there is a difference: it is said this is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, and it is said the view of all (the school), and this is the most correct. The wording of al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that it is not divided until they establish evidence of ownership because it is possible the ownership is in the hand of someone else, end.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn stating that division is permitted in movable property (inherited) and in purchased immovable property without requiring proof of ownership. The commentator explains that this is due to prevailing custom (urf) and the underlying meaning (ma'na) that such property is typically under joint ownership. Additionally, if people claim ownership without specifying how they acquired it, the division is still allowed because it is not a judgment against an absent third party; it only affects those present. There is an internal Hanafi difference: some attribute this lenient view only to Imam Abu Hanifa, others say it is the consensus of the school—the latter being stronger. However, the wording of al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad requires proof of ownership, cautioning that the property might actually belong to someone else. This shows the variety of transmitted positions within the school.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property that can be transferred without damage.
عقار مشتري (aqar mushtara): Immovable property acquired by purchase (as opposed to inheritance).
قسمة (qisma): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the relied-upon position regarding division of inherited movable property when the owners do not prove ownership?
A) It is not divided until proof is established
B) It is divided upon their statement without proof
C) It is divided only if a judge orders it
D) It is divided only if all heirs are present

Key Takeaway
Inherited movables and purchased immovables may be divided among co-owners by mutual consent without formal proof, based on customary practice and the absence of harm to third parties.

Division with Absent Partners: Representation and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on three scenarios where division is prohibited, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division when a partner is absent, distinguish between purchase and inheritance, and evaluate Abu Yusuf's counter-position on appointing a representative.

Core Idea
Division requires both parties present or proper representation; absence of a representative invalidates the judgment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical problem: what happens when jointly owned property needs to be divided but one of the partners or heirs is absent? The Hanafi school distinguishes between purchase (where each owner's title is independent) and inheritance (where ownership is derived from the deceased). The main position prohibits division unless both parties are present or adequately represented, but Abu Yusuf permits the judge to appoint a representative for the absent. Understanding this distinction is crucial for handling property division in inheritance and sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited scenarios
The matn lists three cases where division is not allowed: (1) purchasers with one absent, (2) property in the hand of an absent heir, (3) only one heir present.
These are the core cases to commit to memory.
2
Understand the core rationale for prohibition
The commentator explains that in purchase, each owner acquired new direct ownership, so the present cannot represent the absent. In inheritance, representation is possible through the deceased, but if property is in the absent's hand or only one heir is present, division still fails due to lack of proper representation.
The key is whether the absent party has a representative (khasm).
3
Analyze the exception: when property in absent's hand equals his share
If the part in the absent's hand is equal to or less than his share, the division may not involve taking anything from him, so the prohibition might not apply. This is a nuance from the commentator.
This exception is limited and requires careful calculation.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Abu Yusuf holds that the judge can appoint a representative for the absent, making division valid even without the absent's presence. This includes cases of inheritance and purchase.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi difference.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical implications
The relied-upon position is the main one: division is not allowed in the three scenarios. Abu Yusuf's view is recorded but not acted upon in general fatwa.
Practically, this means delaying division until all parties are present or properly represented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولو كانوا مشترين وغاب أحدهم أو كان العقار في يد الوارث الغائب أو حضر وارث واحد لم يقسم) يعني لا يقسم المال المشترك مع غيبة بعضهم؛ أما في الشراء فلأن الملك الثابت ملك جديد بسبب مباشرة ولهذا لا يرد بالعيب على بائعه فلا يصلح الحاضر أن يكون خصماً على الغائب بخلاف الإرث لأن الملك الثابت فيه ملك خلافه حتى يرد بالعيب فيما اشتراه المورث ويصير مغروراً بشراء المورث فانتصب أحدهما خصماً عن الميت فيما في يد والآخر عن نفسه فصارت القسمة قضاء بحضرة المتخاصمين فيصح القضاء بقيام البينة على خصمه. وفي الشراء قامت على خصم غائب فلا يقبل. وأما إذا كان العقار في يد الوارث الغائب فلأن القسمة قضاء على الغائب بإخراج الشيء من يده من غير خصم عنه فلا يجوز، وكذا إذا كان بعضه في يده والباقي في يد الحاضر، وكذا إذا كان في يد مودعه أو مستعيره أو في يد الصغير لأن المودع والصغير ليسا بخصم، ولا فرق في هذا إقامة البينة وعدمها في الصحيح ا.هـ. فإن قلت : التعليل في قولهم إذا كان شيء منه في يد الصغير أو الغائب يكون قضاء بإخراجه من يده لك أن تقول هذا يستقيم إذا كان كله أو كان البعض الذي في يد الصغير أو الغائب زائداً على قدر حصته ما إذا كان قدر حصته من الدار أو أقل فلا يظهر أن فيه قضاء على الصغير والغائب بإخراج شيء مما كان في يده بل يلزم إبقاء ما كان في يده صورة التساوي وزيادة شيء عليه فيما كان في يد الحاضرين في صورة النقصان ا هـ . وأما إذا حضر وارث واحد فلأنه لا يصلح أن يكون مخاصماً ومخاصماً فلا يصلح أن يكون مقاسماً ومقاسماً لا بد من حضور شخصين على ما بينا؛ هذا الرواية. وعن أبي يوسف أن القاضي ينصب عن الغائب خصماً وتقام البينة، ولو حضر صغير وكبير نصب وصياً عن الصغير وقسم إذا أقيمت البينة، وكذا إذا حضر وارث وموصى له بالثلث في الدار وطلب القسمة وأقاما البينة على الإرث والوصية يقسم لأن الموصى له شريك في الدار فصار كواحد من الورثة فانتصب عن نفسه والوارث عن الميت وبقية الورثة فصار كما إذا حضر وارثان ولو حضر الموصى له وحده لا يقسم؛ ذكره في الذخيرة. وفي النهاية : إنما ينصب القاضي وصياً عن الصغير إذا كان حاضراً بخلاف الغائب. وفي المحيط : ولو كانت مشتركة بالشراء فجرى فيها الميراث بأن مات واحد منهم لا يقسم إذا حضر البعض لأن الوارث لم يقم مقام المورث في الشركة الأولى بالشراء فينظر في الشركة الأولى؛ فإن كانت بالميراث يقوم الثاني مقام الأول، وإن كانت بالشراء لا يقوم.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And if they were purchasers and one of them is absent, or the property was in the hand of the absent heir, or one heir is present, he does not divide' meaning he does not divide the jointly owned property when some are absent. As for purchase, because the established ownership is a new ownership due to direct transaction, and for this reason it is not returned due to a defect to its seller, so the present person cannot be a representative against the absent party, contrary to inheritance because the established ownership in it is a different ownership such that it can be returned due to a defect in what the testator purchased, and he becomes deceived by the testator's purchase. So one of them acts as a representative against the deceased regarding what is in his hand, and the other acts for himself, so the division becomes a judgment in the presence of litigants, so the judgment is valid by establishing evidence against his opponent. In purchase, the evidence was established against an absent opponent, so it is not accepted. As for when the property is in the hand of the absent heir, because the division is a judgment against the absent by taking something out of his hand without a representative for him, so it is not permissible. Likewise if part of it is in his hand and the rest in the hand of the present person. Likewise if it is in the hand of his depositary or borrower or in the hand of a minor, because the depositary and minor are not representatives. There is no difference in this between establishing evidence and not, according to the correct view, end. If you say: the reasoning in their statement that if something of it is in the hand of the minor or absent, it is a judgment to take it out of his hand, you could say this is consistent if it is all of it, or if the part in the hand of the minor or absent exceeds his share. But if it is his share or less, it does not appear that there is a judgment against the minor and absent to take something from his hand; rather, leaving what is in his hand is necessary in the case of equality, and an increase over it in what is in the hands of the present in the case of deficiency, end. As for when one heir is present, because he cannot be both litigant and opponent, so he cannot be both a divider and a participant; two persons must be present, as we explained. This is the narration. And from Abu Yusuf that the judge appoints a representative for the absent and evidence is established. And if a minor and an adult are present, he appoints a guardian for the minor and divides if evidence is established. Likewise if an heir and a legatee of one-third of the house are present and request division and establish evidence of inheritance and bequest, he divides because the legatee is a partner in the house, so he becomes like one of the heirs, acting for himself and the heir acts for the deceased and the remaining heirs, so it is as if two heirs are present. But if only the legatee is present, he does not divide, as mentioned in al-Dhakhira. In al-Nihaya: the judge appoints a guardian for the minor only if he is present, unlike the absent. In al-Muhit: if it was jointly owned by purchase, then inheritance occurred in it such that one of them died, he does not divide if some are present because the heir does not take the place of the testator in the first company by purchase. So he looks at the first company: if it was by inheritance, the second takes the place of the first; if by purchase, he does not.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn covering three scenarios where division is not allowed: (1) when property is purchased and one partner is absent, (2) when inherited property is in the hand of an absent heir, and (3) when only one heir is present. The commentator explains the rationale: in purchase, each owner acquired a new direct ownership, so the present owner cannot represent the absent; in inheritance, the heirs derive ownership from the deceased, so one heir can act as a representative against the deceased regarding the share in his possession, making division a judgment with both sides present. This distinction affects whether evidence against an absent person is accepted. If the property is physically in the hand of an absent heir, division would involve taking property from his possession without a representative, which is invalid. This applies even if only part is in his hand, unless the part is equal to or less than his share, in which case it might not be a judgment against him. Regarding only one heir present, he cannot act as both litigant and opponent, so two persons are needed. However, Abu Yusuf holds that the judge can appoint a representative for the absent. If a legatee is present along with an heir, that counts as two parties. The passage also discusses the difference between inheritance and purchase in terms of representation after death.

Key Terms
شراء (shira'): Purchase transaction creating new direct ownership.
ميراث (mirath): Inheritance, where ownership is derived from the deceased.
موصى له (musa lahu): Legatee, a person entitled to a bequest (wasiyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the main Hanafi position, why is division not allowed when only one heir is present?
A) Because the present heir cannot represent the deceased.
B) Because the present heir cannot act as both litigant and opponent.
C) Because inheritance requires all heirs to be present.
D) Because the judge has no jurisdiction.

Key Takeaway
Division of joint property requires both parties present or proper representation; absence of a representative renders the judgment invalid, and Abu Yusuf's allowance for judge-appointed representatives is a minority view.

Partition of Building on Another's Land: Absent Owner
Ruling: two builders can partition the building even if land owner is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partition of a building built with permission on another's land when the owner is absent, and identify the condition that triggers permissibility and the limitation on compulsion.

Core Idea
Builders own the building; they may partition it even if the landowner is absent, but none can be forced.

In Hanafi fiqh, a building constructed on another's land with the owner's permission belongs to the builder, not the landowner. This separation of ownership matters when the builders wish to divide the building among themselves. This lesson examines a ruling from al-Tajrid that clarifies the rights of builders when the landowner is absent and one builder refuses partition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is partition (qisma) of a building (bina) that was built by two persons on another's land. The building was erected with the landowner's permission.
Permission is key; without it, the ruling may differ.
2
Determine the ownership of the building
In Hanafi law, the building is owned by the builders, not the landowner, because they built with permission and the landowner's consent transfers ownership of the structure to them.
This separation of land and building ownership is a distinctive Hanafi principle.
3
Apply the ruling: partition allowed despite owner's absence
Since the building belongs to the builders, the landowner's absence does not hinder partition. The builders may divide the building between themselves as they wish.
The landowner's rights in the land are unaffected; only the building is partitioned.
4
Identify the limitation: no compulsion
If one of the builders refuses to partition, he cannot be forced. Partition is not compulsory when it would cause hardship to any party.
This contrasts with some cases where partition is obligatory if it is beneficial and non-harmful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التجريد : ولو بنى رجلان في أرض لرجل بإذنه ثم أرادا قسمة البناء ومؤاجر الأرض غائب فلهما ذلك، فإن أبى أحدهما لم يجبر على القسمة
And in al-Tajrid: If two men built on a man's land with his permission, then they want to partition the building while the land owner is absent, they have that right. If one of them refuses, he is not compelled to partition.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding partition of a building erected on someone else's land with permission. The building is owned by the builders, not the landowner. Therefore, the absence of the landowner does not prevent the builders from partitioning the building among themselves. However, if one of the builders refuses to partition, he is not forced, because partition of the building is not compulsory when it would cause hardship. This ruling reflects the principle that partition is only compelled when it results in benefit for all parties without significant harm.

Key Terms
بناء (bina): A structure erected on land, treated as separate property from land in ownership

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can two builders partition a building on another's land even if the landowner is absent?
A) They built without permission
B) They built with the landowner's permission
C) The landowner is present
D) One builder refuses

Key Takeaway
Builders who build with permission own the building; they may partition it in the owner's absence, but no builder can be forced to divide.

Effect of Istihqaq after Partition before Possession
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istihqaq after partition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the effect of istihqaq after partition before possession and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Partition before possession is valid; the dispute is whether istihqaq in one half nullifies the sale in the other.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a scenario where a buyer purchases half a house and partitions it with the seller before taking possession. The key question: if a third party later claims ownership of one of the halves, what happens to the sale of the other half? The Hanafi school has two positions, and understanding their practical consequences is essential for navigating real estate transactions with title defects.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the agreed rule
Note that all parties agree: partition before possession is valid. The dispute is only about remedies after a claim.
2
Identify the triggering event
Istihqaq (successful claim) of a half occurs after partition. Determine which half is claimed – the buyer's or the seller's – and whether further sales have taken place.
3
Distinguish the two positions
Abu Yusuf and Zufar: the sale is void in the claimed half, and the buyer has options to adjust the deal. Abu Hanifa: the sale in the unclaimed half remains valid; the buyer must seek compensation from the seller or the claimant.
The text presents both as valid Hanafi views.
4
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Under Abu Yusuf, the buyer may reduce the seller's share; under Abu Hanifa, the seller's share is protected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن الحسن : رجل اشترى من آخر نصف دار ثم قاسمه قبل أن يقبضها جازت القسمة، فإن استحق النصف الذي في يد المشتري بطل البيع فيه والمشتري بالخيار إن شاء أخذ نصف ما في يد البائع بحصته من الثمن، وإن شاء ترك. وإن استحق نصف البائع بطل البيع فيه والمشتري بالخيار إن شاء أخذ النصف من النصف الذي صار له بالحصة من الثمن، وإن شاء ترك. ولو لم يستحق شيئاً حتى باع المشتري النصف الذي صار له ثم استحق النصف الذي صار للمشتري يبطل البيع فيه وكان للمشتري أن يأخذ نصف ما باع البائع ويبطل البيع في نصفه، وكذا إن باع كل واحد منهما نصيبه ثم استحق أحد النصيبين فالجواب فيه كالجواب فيما باع أحدهما، وهذا كله على قياس قول أبي يوسف وزفر رحمهما الله تعالى وبه أخذ الحسن قال : وفي قول أبي حنيفة أي النصفين استحق جاز البيع في الآخر وله أن من الذي يبيع اشتراها منه قبل القبض ومن الأجنبي.
And from al-Hasan: A man bought half a house from another, then partitioned with him before taking possession. The partition is valid. If the half that came into the buyer's hand is claimed (by a third party), the sale is void in that half, and the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take half of what is in the seller's hand in proportion to his payment, and if he wishes, he may leave it. And if the seller's half is claimed, the sale is void in that half, and the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take half of the half that became his in proportion to his payment, and if he wishes, he may leave it. And if nothing was claimed until the buyer sold the half that became his, then the half that became the buyer's was claimed, the sale of that half is void, and the buyer may take half of what the seller sold and void the sale in his half. Likewise, if each of them sold his share, then one of the two shares was claimed, the answer is the same as when one of them sold. All this is according to the analogy of the saying of Abu Yusuf and Zufar, may Allah have mercy on them, and al-Hasan adopted it. He said: According to the saying of Abu Hanifa, whichever of the two halves is claimed, the sale is valid in the other, and he has the right to take from the one who sold [the claimed share] before possession and from the outsider.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a claim of ownership (istihqaq) after partition of a purchased property before possession. According to Abu Yusuf and Zufar (and adopted by al-Hasan), partition before possession is valid. If later one of the partitioned halves is claimed by a third party, the sale is void in that half, but the buyer has remedial options (khiyar) to adjust the deal. The details depend on whether the claimed half was originally the seller's or the buyer's, and whether further sales occurred. Imam Abu Hanifa holds a different view: regardless of which half is claimed, the sale in the other half remains valid, and the buyer may claim compensation from the seller or the outsider. This dispute impacts the rights of the buyer and seller in cases of defective title.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): A successful claim by a third party that property rightfully belongs to them
خيار (khiyar): An option or right to rescind or modify a contract upon the occurrence of a defect or claim

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Zufar, if the seller's half is claimed after partition before possession, what option does the buyer have?
A) The buyer can take the entire property
B) The buyer can take half of the half that became his in proportion to his payment
C) The buyer can only demand a refund
D) The buyer has no option; the sale is void

Key Takeaway
Partition before possession is valid; the effect of istihqaq on the unclaimed half is disputed between Abu Hanifa (sale remains valid) and Abu Yusuf/Zufar (buyer has options).

Conditions for Compulsory Partition: Benefit and Harm Scenarios
Rulings on compulsory partition based on benefit/harm scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios where compulsory partition is or is not ordered by the judge, and apply the rule to given co-ownership cases.

Core Idea
Compulsory partition requires benefit to all; if some are harmed, only the large share owner can compel.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on compulsory partition (qismat jabbariyya). The judge may compel partition only when it benefits every co-owner. When partition harms all, it requires consent; when some benefit and some are harmed, only the owner of the larger share can demand it. We also learn the rule for chattels: only items of the same type are subject to compulsory division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The text classifies cases into: (1) all benefit → judge compels; (2) all harmed → no compulsion, only with consent; (3) some benefit, some harmed (due to small share) → only large share owner can compel.
2
Understand the rationale for each scenario
Partition is meant to complete benefit; when it harms, the request is considered obstinate (ta'annut), so the judge does not respond. For the mixed case, the large owner asks for his right to exclusive use, while the small owner's request is harmful to himself.
The ruling is based on preventing harm (darar) and ensuring utility.
3
Examine the rule for chattels (uruud)
Compulsory partition applies only to chattels of the same type (jins wahid). Different types and jewels are not subject to compulsory partition due to disparity in value.
This limits the scope of qismat jabbariyya to homogeneous goods.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on the judge's role when all consent
When all parties consent to a harmful partition, there are two narrations: one says the judge does not officiate (preferred), another says he does. The preferred view is that the judge refrains from engaging in a harmful act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تضرر الكل لم يقسم إلا برضاهم وإن انتفع البعض وتضرر البعض لقلة حظه قسم بطلب ذي الكثير فقط ويقسم العروض من جنس واحد ولا يقسم الجنسين والجواهر قال رحمه الله : (وقسم القاضي بطلب أحدهم لو انتفع كل بنصيبه) لأن فيه تكميل المنفعة إذا كان كل واحد منهم ينتفع بنصيبه بعد القسمة وكانت القسمة حقاً لهم فوجب على القاضي إجابتهم. قال في العناية : يعني يقسم جبراً ومراده إذا كان من جنس واحد لأن فيه معنى الإقرار التفاوت المقاصد . قال رحمه الله : (وإن تضرر الكل لم يقسم إلا برضاهم) وذلك كما لو طلبوا قسمة البئر والرحى والحائط والحمام لأن القسمة لتكميل المنفعة، وفي قسمة هذا تفويت فيعود على موضعه بالنقص، ولأن الطالب للقسمة متعنت ويريد إدخال الضرر على غيره فلا يجبه الحاكم إلى ذلك لأنه اشتغال بما لا يفيد بل بما يضر ويجوز بالتراضي لأن الحق لهم وهم أعرف بحاجتهم لكن القاضي لا يباشر ذلك وإن طلبوه منه لأن القاضي لا يشتغل بما لا فائدة فيه لا سيما إذا كان فيه إضرار وإضاعة مال لأن ذلك حرام ولا يمنعهم منه. اهـ. كلام الشارح. لكن ظاهر المتن أن القاضي يقسم عند رضاهم. وفي الينابيع والذخيرة: ذكر شيخ الإسلام أن القاضي لا يقسم وبعض المشايخ قال يقسم فظهر أن في المسألة روايتين. قال رحمه الله : (وإن انتفع البعض وتضرر البعض لقلة حظه قسم بطلب ذي الكثير فقط) يعني يقسم بطلب صاحب الكثير ؛ كذا ذكره صاحب الخصاف، صاحب الكثير يطلب من القاضي أن يخصه بالانتفاع بملكه ويمنع غيره عن الانتفاع بملكه وهذا منه طلب الحق والإنصاف فإن له أن يمنع غيره من الانتفاع بملكه فوجب على القاضي أن يجيبه إلى ذلك، ولا يعتبر ضرر الآخر لأنه يريد أن ينتفع بملك غيره فلا يمكن من . ولو طلب صاحب القليل أنه لا ينتفع بحقه مع أنه متعنت في طلب القسمة فلا يشتغل القاضي بما لا يفيد وذكر الجصاص أنه إن طلب صاحب القليل قسم، وإن طلب صاحب الكثير لا يقسم وذكر الحاكم أيهم طلب القسمة يقسم القاضي والأصح ما ذكر الخصاف لأن القاضي يجب عليه إيصال الحق إلى مستحقه ولا يلزمه أن يجيبهم إلى إضرار أنفسهم.
If all are harmed, it is not partitioned except with their consent. And if some benefit and some are harmed due to a small share, it is partitioned only at the request of the one with the large share. And chattels of one type are partitioned, but two types and jewels are not partitioned. He (the author) said: (And the judge partitions at the request of one of them if each benefits from his share) because it completes the benefit when each of them benefits from his share after partition, and partition is their right, so it is obligatory on the judge to respond to them. He said in al-'Inaya: He means he partitions compulsorily, and his intention is when it is of one type, because there is the meaning of acknowledging the difference in objectives. He said: (And if all are harmed, it is not partitioned except with their consent) such as if they request partition of a well, a mill, a wall, or a bathhouse, because partition is for completing benefit, and in partitioning these there is loss, so it returns to its place with deficiency. And because the one requesting partition is obstinate and wants to bring harm to others, so the judge does not respond to that, as it is engagement in what is not beneficial but harmful. However, it is permissible with mutual consent because the right is theirs and they know their need better. But the judge does not undertake it even if they ask him, because the judge does not engage in what has no benefit, especially if it involves harm and wasting wealth, as that is haram, and he does not prevent them from it. End of the commentator's words. But the apparent meaning of the matn is that the judge partitions when they consent. In al-Yanabi' and al-Dhakhira: Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that the judge does not partition, and some mashayikh said he does. So it appears there are two narrations in the issue. He said: (And if some benefit and some are harmed due to a small share, it is partitioned only at the request of the one with the large share.) Meaning it is partitioned at the request of the large share owner. As mentioned by the author of al-Khassaf: The large share owner asks the judge to allocate him the benefit of his property and prevent others from benefiting from his property, and this is a request for right and fairness, because he has the right to prevent others from benefiting from his property, so it is obligatory on the judge to respond to him. The harm to the other is not considered because he wants to benefit from another's property, so he is not enabled to do so. And if the small share owner requests, he does not benefit from his right since he is obstinate in requesting partition, so the judge does not engage in what is not beneficial. Al-Jassas mentioned that if the small share owner requests, it is partitioned; if the large share owner requests, it is not. And al-Hakim said whichever of them requests partition, the judge partitions. The most correct is what al-Khassaf mentioned, because the judge must deliver rights to their owners, but he is not obliged to answer them to harm themselves.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This matn with its sharh presents the core conditions for compulsory partition (qismat al-iftitah) in Hanafi law. Three scenarios: 1) If every co-owner benefits from partition (e.g., a large house divisible into separate flats), the judge compels partition at the request of any one co-owner. 2) If all are harmed (e.g., a well or mill that loses value if divided), partition is not compulsory; it requires consent, and even then some scholars say the judge should not officiate it due to lack of benefit. 3) If some benefit and some are harmed due to a small share, only the owner of the larger share can compel partition; the small share owner cannot, as his request would be harmful to himself. The commentary also notes a dispute: whether the judge partitions when all consent (two narrations). The preferred view is that the judge does not officiate a harmful partition. Additionally, partition of chattels (uruud) is only for items of the same type; mixed types and jewels are not subject to compulsory partition because value differs too greatly.

Key Terms
قسمة جبرية (qismat jabbariyya): Compulsory partition ordered by the judge even if some co-owners object
عروض (uruud): Chattels; movable goods (as opposed to real estate)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the judge compel partition of chattels?
A) For any chattels regardless of type
B) Only for chattels of the same type
C) Only for real estate, never chattels
D) For chattels only if they are jewels

Key Takeaway
Compulsory partition is not absolute; it depends on benefit: if all benefit, judge compels; if all harmed, no; if some benefit and some harm, only large share owner can compel.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Forced Division of Real Estate
Intra-Hanafi dispute on forced division of real estate types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on forced division of real estate and state the mufta bihi position regarding combining different types of properties.

Core Idea
In forced division, Imam Abu Hanifa treats each house as a distinct type, preventing combination without consent, while the Sahibayn allow it for benefit.

The forced division of shared property (qismat al-shuyu') requires careful classification of assets. This passage explores whether a judge can combine different parcels of real estate into one share to avoid fragmentation. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between the Imam and his two disciples, with implications for the rights of co-owners.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling context
The act is the forced division of shared real estate (e.g., houses, estates, shops) by a judge. The ruling under dispute is whether the judge can combine different properties into one share for a partner.
2
State the Imam's position and his dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that houses are different types (ajnas) due to differences in location, neighbors, and proximity to the mosque. This makes forced combination unjust because equalization is impossible. Each partner must receive a separate property or consent to combination.
The Imam's dalil is based on the purpose (maqsad) of each property being unique.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that houses in the same city are one type because they share the name and form. Combining shares prevents fragmentation and benefits the partners.
The Sahibayn's dalil emphasizes the commonality of name and form.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: under the Imam, each partner must get a separate property; under the Sahibayn, the judge can combine. The author sides with the Imam, so the mufta bihi is the stricter view, requiring consent for combination.
For mixed types (e.g., house and shop), the disagreement is even stronger, but the Imam's view prevails in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (دور) مشتركة أو دار وضيعة أو دار وحانوت قسم كل على حدة أما الدور المشتركة فالمذكور ههنا قول الإمام. وقالا : تقسم الدور بعضها في بعض إذا كانت في مصر واحد وكانت القسمة أصلح لهم لأنهم جنس واحد نظراً إلى اتحاد الاسم والصورة وأصل السكنى جنسان نظراً إلى اختلاف الأغراض وتفاوت السكني. وإذا قسم كل دار على حدة ربما يتضرر لقلة نصيبه. وللإمام أن الدور أجناس مختلفة لاختلاف المقصود باعتبار المحال والجيران والقرب من المسجد فكان اختلافاً فاحشاً فلا يمكن التعديل في القسمة فلا يجوز جمع نصيب كل واحد في دار إلا بالتراضي والإبل والبقر والغنم يقسم كل جنس منه بانفراده ولا يجمع بين الأجناس كما ذكرنا بخلاف الدور والمنازل المتلازقة كالبيوت والساحة كالدور لأنه بين البيت والدار فأخذ حظه من كل واحد منهما. والدور في مصرين تقسم بالإجماع، وأما الدور والضيعة والدار والحانوت فلاختلاف الجنس؛ ذكره الخصاف. وفي رواية الأصل ما يشير إلى أنه يجوز اهـ.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Houses) shared, or a house and an estate, or a house and a shop, each is divided separately. As for shared houses, what is mentioned here is the saying of the Imam. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: houses are divided among each other if they are in one city and the division is more beneficial for them, because they are one type in view of the unity of name and form, and the origin of residence is one type? [Actually: 'and the origin of residence is two types?'] No, the Arabic says: 'وأصل السكنى جنسان نظراً إلى اختلاف الأغراض وتفاوت السكني' meaning 'and the origin of residence is two types due to difference of purposes and variation of dwelling.' [This is the Imam's view]. If each house is divided separately, perhaps one suffers due to the smallness of his share. The Imam holds that houses are different types due to difference of purpose considering locations, neighbors, and proximity to the mosque, so the difference is gross; equalization in division is not possible, so it is not permissible to gather each partner's share in one house except by mutual consent. Camels, cows, and sheep each type is divided separately, and types are not combined as we mentioned, unlike houses and adjoining dwellings like rooms and courtyard like houses because it is between room and house, so he takes his share from each. Houses in two cities are divided by consensus. As for a house and an estate, or a house and a shop, due to difference of type; al-Khassaf mentioned that. And in one narration from al-Asl, there is indication that it is permissible. End.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage continues the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the forced division of real estate. The matn states that shared houses, or a house with an estate, or a house with a shop, are each divided separately, meaning the judge does not combine different types into one share. The commentary explains that for shared houses (all houses), Imam Abu Hanifa holds that they are different types because each house has unique characteristics (location, neighbors, proximity to mosque) causing gross disparity, so forced division combining shares is not allowed; each must receive his share in a separate house, or by mutual consent. The Sahibayn argue that houses in the same city are of one type because they share the name and form, and it may be more beneficial to combine shares to avoid small fragments. However, the Imam's view prevails. For different categories (house vs. estate, house vs. shop), there is stronger disagreement; al-Khassaf reports it is not allowed due to different types, but a narration from al-Asl indicates permissibility. The passage also compares to animals: each species is divided separately, not mixed.

Key Terms
الدور (al-dur): Houses (plural of دار).
الضيعة (al-day'a): An estate or agricultural land.
الحانوت (al-hanut): A shop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the main reason houses cannot be combined in forced division?
A) Because they are immovable property.
B) Because they differ in purpose due to unique characteristics like location and neighbors.
C) Because the Quran explicitly prohibits it.
D) Because the Sahibayn disagree.

Key Takeaway
In forced division, the Hanafi school (mufta bihi) treats each house as a distinct type, preventing combination without mutual consent.

The Divider's Duties in Dividing Common Property
Ruling statement of the divider's procedure with a dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the steps the divider takes when dividing shared property and explain the ruling when division involves loss of benefit.

Core Idea
The divider must evaluate, label, and draw lots — equitable division requires procedural fairness.

When co-owners wish to partition their joint property, a qasim (divider) is appointed. This passage from Kenz al-Daqa'iq outlines his responsibilities: from valuing structures to drawing lots for allocation. It also addresses a key nuance: what if the division itself causes a loss of benefit? Understanding this procedure ensures that the division is legally valid and just for all parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divider's responsibilities
Read the passage and list the specific actions the divider must perform: evaluate buildings, separate shares with paths and watering rights, label shares, write names, draw lots.
These steps ensure each co-owner receives a fair portion.
2
Understand the valuation and separation
Note that 'evaluating the buildings' means assessing their worth, and 'separating each share with its path and watering place' ensures each share has necessary appurtenances.
This prevents future disputes over access rights.
3
Recognize the use of lots (qur'ah)
The divider labels shares as first, second, third, writes the partners' names, and draws lots. This random assignment is a just method to allocate shares without bias.
Drawing lots is not gambling; it is a recognized equitable tool in Hanafi law.
4
Note the dispute about loss of benefit
The passage mentions two narrations: some say the judge should not divide if it causes loss of benefit (safah), while others permit it if the partners consent and there is some benefit.
This reflects the principle of avoiding harm (darar) balanced against consent.
5
Distinguish the two opinions
The first opinion restricts the judge's authority; the second allows division with consent. The author (Kenz al-Daqa'iq) hints at the latter because it involves benefit.
Later Hanafi practice often follows the consent-based narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقوم البناء ويفرز كل نصيب بطريقه وشربه ويلقب الأنصباء بالأول والثاني والثالث ويكتب أسماءهم ويقرع فمن خرج اسمه أو لا فله السهم الأول ومن خرج ثانياً فله يقسم لأنها تضمنت تفويت منفعة وليس للقاضي ذلك لأنه يكون سفهاً يمكنه، وفي رواية يقسم لأنهم رضوا بذلك وإليه أشار في الكتاب لأنه فيه نوع منفعة؛ كذا في المحيط.
And he values the buildings, and separates each share with its path and its watering place, and labels the shares as first, second, third, and writes their names and draws lots. Whoever's name comes out first gets the first share, and whoever comes out second gets... [it is divided] because it involves loss of benefit, and the judge does not have that because it would be foolishness that can [be avoided?]. And in one narration, it is divided because they are pleased with that, and the author pointed to it in the book because there is a kind of benefit in it; like this in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn (Kenz al-Daqa'iq) and its commentary. It outlines the duties of the divider (qasim) when dividing common property. He must evaluate buildings, separate each share with its specific path and watering right, label the shares numerically, write the names of the partners, and then draw lots. The text notes a dispute: if division involves loss of benefit (e.g., dividing a right of way that becomes unusable), some say the judge should not divide because it is foolish to spoil property; another narration allows division if the partners agree, because there is some benefit. This is quoted from al-Muhit. The commentary does not discuss proofs but states the rulings.

Key Terms
القاسم (al-qasim): The person appointed to divide common property among co-owners.
القرعة (al-qur'ah): Drawing lots to assign shares randomly but fairly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Assign it to the first name drawn regardless of value
B) Separate it with its path and watering place
C) Sell it to the highest bidder
D) Only label it if the partners request

Key Takeaway
The divider must follow a set procedure—evaluate, separate, label, and draw lots—and division involving loss of benefit requires partner consent.

Dividing Shared Water Sources in Hanafi Law
Rulings from multiple Hanafi works on dividing water rights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions under which a shared water source (qanat, well, river) can be divided among partners, and apply these rules to practical irrigation scenarios.

Core Idea
Water without land stays shared; water with land may be divided if no harm results.

The division of water rights (shirb) is a nuanced area of Hanafi muamalat. This lesson examines key rulings from authoritative Hanafi texts on when a qanat, well, or river can be physically divided among co-owners, and when they must remain joint. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for resolving disputes over irrigation and water access.

Guided Path
1
Identify the asset and its attachment to land
Determine whether the water source (qanat, well, river) is attached to land or exists independently. This is the primary factor governing divisibility.
If no land is attached, division is generally not permitted.
2
Assess alternative water availability
Check if each partner can obtain water from another source. If yes, then the entire water source along with land can be divided.
This comes from al-Khulasa ruling.
3
Apply the ruling based on these factors
Synthesize the conditions: if land is attached and alternative water is unavailable, divide only the land; if alternative water is available, divide everything; if no land attached, no division.
The rulings from Tatarakhaniyyah and al-Asl guide this.
4
Note the exceptional case of dividing by cubits
From al-Nawadir: if a well is divided by estimating cubits, it is allowed because variation in quality is minimal.
This shows flexibility when precise measurement is impractical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التتارخانية : وإذا كانت قناة أو بئر أو نهر وليس معه أرض فأراد بعض الشركاء القسمة فإنها لا تقسم، وإذا كانت أرض لها شرب قسم الأرض وترك الشرب والقناة والبئر كالشركة . وفي الخلاصة : ولكل منهما شربة فإن كان يقدر كل واحد منهما أن يجعل أرضه شرباً من موضع آخر قسم ذلك كله فيما بينهم. وفي الأصل لو كانت أنهاراً وآبار الأرض مختلفة قسم الآبار والعيون والأراضي اهـ. وفي النوادر : ولو قسم البئر بالجبال جاز لأن التفاوت فيها قليل اهـ.
And in al-Tatarakhaniyyah: If there is a qanat, well, or river with no land attached, and some partners want to divide it, it is not divided. And if there is land with irrigation rights, the land is divided and the irrigation right is left, and the qanat and well are like the partnership. In al-Khulasa: Each of them has a watering turn; if each of them can make his land watered from another place, then all of that is divided among them. In al-Asl: If there are rivers and wells of varying land [quality], the wells, springs, and lands are divided. In al-Nawadir: If a well is divided by [estimating] the cubits, it is permissible because the variation is small.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage gathers multiple fiqh references on dividing water sources. The general rule: if a water source (qanat, well, river) has no attached land, it cannot be divided among partners because the benefit is joint and cannot be partitioned without loss. If there is land with an irrigation right (shirb), the land is divided but the water right remains shared. However, if each partner can independently obtain water from another source, then all can be divided. In al-Asl (by Imam Muhammad), if lands with varying water sources are involved, all are divided together. The Nawadir reports that estimating a well's share by cubits is acceptable because the difference in quality is minimal. These rulings show the Hanafi principle of considering practicality and harm in division.

Key Terms
قناة (qanat): Underground canal
شرب (shirb): Irrigation right or turn
قسمة (qisma): Division or partition of jointly owned property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khulasa, when can both land and water rights be divided among partners?
A) When each partner can water his land from another source
B) When the water source is a river
C) When all partners agree
D) When the land is of equal quality

Key Takeaway
A shared water source without land remains undivided; with land, division depends on alternative water access and quality variation.
