Division of Houses: Imam vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing houses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on combining houses in division and state the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Houses are different genera by location; Sahibayn see them as one genus in a city.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a dispute among the Hanafi founders regarding whether different houses can be combined in a single division. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals how jurists balance legal categorization against practical benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ on whether multiple houses can be combined into a single division.
The matn states Imam's view; the commentary explains the dispute.
2
Examine the reasoning for each position
Imam focuses on differences in location, neighbors, and proximity to mosque, making houses different genera. Sahibayn focus on unity of name and form, considering them one genus.
This is a classic example of ta'lil in fiqh.
3
Consider the exceptions and analogies
Note that livestock must be divided separately by species. Attached dwellings (like rooms and courtyards) are treated like one house. Houses in different cities are divided separately by consensus.
These analogies help define the scope of the dispute.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Imam, each partner gets a share in each house, potentially small shares in multiple properties. Under Sahibayn, partners can receive whole houses if it is more beneficial.
This practical difference affects the outcome of division.
5
Determine the operative view
The matn supports Imam's view, but the narration from al-Asl indicates permissibility, showing flexibility.
The mufta bihi may vary by context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (دور) مشتركة أو دار وضيعة أو دار وحانوت قسم كل على حدة أما الدور المشتركة فالمذكور ههنا قول الإمام. وقالا : تقسم الدور بعضها في بعض إذا كانت في مصر واحد وكانت القسمة أصلح لهم لأنهم جنس واحد نظراً إلى اتحاد الاسم والصورة وأصل السكنى جنسان نظراً إلى اختلاف الأغراض وتفاوت السكني. وإذا قسم كل دار على حدة ربما يتضرر لقلة نصيبه. وللإمام أن الدور أجناس مختلفة لاختلاف المقصود باعتبار المحال والجيران والقرب من المسجد فكان اختلافاً فاحشاً فلا يمكن التعديل في القسمة فلا يجوز جمع نصيب كل واحد في دار إلا بالتراضي والإبل والبقر والغنم يقسم كل جنس منه بانفراده ولا يجمع بين الأجناس كما ذكرنا بخلاف الدور والمنازل المتلازقة كالبيوت والساحة كالدور لأنه بين البيت والدار فأخذ حظه من كل واحد منهما. والدور في مصرين تقسم بالإجماع، وأما الدور والضيعة والدار والحانوت فلاختلاف الجنس؛ ذكره الخصاف. وفي رواية الأصل ما يشير إلى أنه جاز اهـ.
He (the author) said: (Houses) shared, or a house and an estate, or a house and a shop, each is divided separately. As for shared houses, what is mentioned here is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Houses can be divided some in place of others if they are in one city and the division is more beneficial for them, because they are one genus considering the unity of name and form. And the origin of dwellings is two types considering difference of purposes and variation of habitation. If each house is divided separately, perhaps harm comes due to smallness of share. For Imam, houses are different genera due to difference of purpose considering locations, neighbors, proximity to mosque, so the difference is great and equitable division is impossible, so it is not permissible to combine each partner's share in one house except by mutual consent. And camels, cows, sheep: each genus is divided separately and not combined with other genera as we mentioned. Unlike houses and attached dwellings like rooms and courtyards, which are like houses because [the partner] is between a house and a dwelling so he takes his portion from each. Houses in two cities are divided by consensus. As for houses and estate, house and shop, it is due to difference of genus; al-Khassaf mentioned it. And in a narration of al-Asl, there is indication that it is permissible.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn (Kenz al-Daqa'iq) states that different types of properties (house, estate, shop) must be divided separately. The commentator explains that this is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) argue that houses of the same city are one genus and can be combined in division if it is more beneficial, avoiding loss from small shares. Imam argues that houses differ in value based on location and purpose, making equitable division impossible without consent. The dispute applies to houses only; for livestock, each species is separate. The text also notes consensus on houses in two cities being divided separately. There is also a narration from al-Asl (the original work of Imam Muhammad) that suggests permissibility of combining, softening the disagreement. The relied-upon view is not explicitly stated here.

Key Terms
دار (dar): House
سكنى (sukna): Dwelling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa on combining different houses in a single division without the consent of all partners?
A) It is permissible if the division is more beneficial.
B) It is not permissible because houses are different genera.
C) It is permissible only if the houses are in the same city.
D) It is impermissible under all circumstances.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has internal disagreement on combining houses in division: Imam requires separate division unless consent, while Sahibayn allow combination if beneficial, reflecting a tension between legal categorization and practical benefit.

The Practical Method of Drawing Lots in Division
Explanation of the drawing lots procedure and its permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of drawing lots for dividing jointly owned property and state the ruling of its permissibility.

Core Idea
Drawing lots in division assigns pre-existing entitlements, not new ones — thus it is not gambling.

In this lesson, we learn the practical procedure for drawing lots (qur'ah) as prescribed by the Hanafi school when partners cannot agree on how to divide property. The passage explains how to calculate shares based on the smallest fraction and how to conduct the random draw. It also establishes that this method is not only permissible but also legitimate according to Quranic precedent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose
Drawing lots is used to please the hearts of the partners and avoid conflict. It is not obligatory; the ruler can divide without it.
The goal is psychological satisfaction, not the creation of rights.
2
Understand the calculation
Determine the smallest share among the partners. Convert all shares to that common denominator. For example, if shares are 1/2, 1/3, 1/6, use 1/6 as the unit.
This ensures equal distribution of units.
3
Prepare the lots
Write each partner's name on a small slip of paper, making them identical. Place them in a sleeve or container.
Slips must be indistinguishable to ensure randomness.
4
Draw the lots
Draw slips one by one. The first name drawn gets the first reserved share, the second gets the second share, and so on.
The order determines which set of units the partner receives.
5
Apply to the example
If the first drawn is the partner with a half share, he receives three sixths from the first share; if drawn second, he receives three sixths from the second share.
Each partner receives his predetermined total in the units assigned to his drawn position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلقب الأنصباء بالأول والثاني والثالث ويكتب أسماءهم ويقرع فمن خرج اسمه أو لا فله السهم الأول ومن خرج ثانياً فله السهم الثاني) والقرعة لتطييب قلوبهم، فلو أقسم الإمام بلا قرعة جاز لأنه في معنى القضاء فيملك الإلزام فيه. وكيفيته أن ينظر إلى أقل الأنصباء فيقدر به آخر السهام حتى إذا كان العقار بين ثلاثة لأحدهم النصف وللآخر الثلث وللآخر السدس جعلها أسداساً لأنه أقل الأنصباء فيكتب أسماء الشركاء في بطاقات ويجعلها شبه البندقة ثم يخرجها حتى إذا نشقت وهي مثل البندقة يدلكها ثم يجعلها في كمه أو وعى فيخرجها واحداً بعد واحد ؛ فمن خرج اسمه أولاً فله السهم الأول، ومن خرج ثانياً فله السهم الثاني، ومن خرج ثالثاً فله السهم الثالث إلى أن ينتهي إلى الأخير، فإن خرج أولاً في المثال الذي ذكرناه اسم صاحب النصف فإن له ثلاثة أسداس من الجانب الملقب بالأول، وإن خرج ثانياً كان له كذلك من الجانب الذي يلي الأول، وإن خرج ثالثاً كان له كذلك من الجانب الذي يلي الثاني، وعلى هذا كل واحد منهم. لا يقال تعليق الاستحقاق بالقرعة قمار وهو حرام ولهذا لم يجز علماؤنا استعمالها في دعوى النسب ودعوى الملك وتعين العتق والمطلقة لأنا نقول : لا يحصل الاستحقاق لأن الاستحقاق كان ثابتاً قبله وكان للقاضي ولاية الزام كل واحد منهم وإنما القمار على زعمهم اسم ما يستحقون به ما لم يكن لهم قبل لا مثل هذه بل هذه مشروعة كما أخبر الله سبحانه وتعالى عن يونس وزكريا عليهم الصلاة والسلام كما قال الله تعالى إذ يلقون أقلامهم أيهم يكفل [آل عمران: 44] الآية وقوله تعالى فساهم فكان من المدحضين [الصافات: 141] الآية . ولقائل أن يقول : بين أول كلامهم وآخره تدافع لأنهم صرحوا أولاً بأن مشروعية استعمال القرعة هنا جواب استحسان والقياس يأبى ذلك ، وقالوا آخراً أن هذا ليس بقمار وبينوا الفرق بينه وبين القمار وذكروا له نظائر في الكتاب والسنة فقد دل على أنه لا يأباه القياس أصلاً بل هو يقتضيه القياس أيضاً فتدافعا اهـ .
And he labels the shares as first, second, third, and writes their names and draws lots. Whoever's name comes out first gets the first share, and whoever comes out second gets the second share. And drawing lots is to please their hearts. So if the ruler divides without lots, it is permissible because it is like a judgment, so he has the authority to compel. Its method: he looks at the smallest share and estimates the last shares accordingly. If the property is among three: one has half, another third, another sixth, he makes it sixths because it is the smallest share. He writes the partners' names on slips, makes them like small balls, then withdraws them. He puts them in his sleeve or container and extracts them one by one. Whoever's name comes out first gets the first share, etc. In the example, if the owner of half comes out first, he gets three sixths from the side labelled first; if second, from the side next to first, etc. It should not be said that linking entitlement to lots is gambling and forbidden, because entitlement was already established before, and the judge has the authority to compel each partner. Gambling is something by which one gains what one had no right to before. This is different; it is legislated as per the Quranic stories of Yunus and Zakariyya. Objection: There is contradiction because at first they say it is istihsan and qiyas rejects it, and later they say it is not gambling and qiyas also supports it. Response: [the text ends with a comment that this is a contradiction, but the author seems to note the objection].
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage provides the practical method of drawing lots for division. The divider calculates shares based on the smallest fraction, writes names on identical slips, and draws them randomly. The text then addresses an objection: that drawing lots is gambling (qimar), which is haram. The response distinguishes: in division, entitlement already exists; the lot only determines which share goes to whom. It is not gambling because no one gains what they didn't already own. Proof is cited from Surah Al 'Imran (the story of Zakariyya) and Surah al-Saffat (the story of Yunus), showing that drawing lots was used by prophets and is thus legislated. The text notes a potential contradiction in earlier Hanafi statements that the procedure is based on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas, while later claims it is also supported by qiyas. This is noted but not fully resolved.

Key Terms
قرعة (qur'ah): Drawing lots
قمار (qimar): Gambling: gaining something of value through chance, where no pre-existing right exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi method of drawing lots for division, what determines the unit of the division?
A) The largest share
B) The smallest share
C) The average share
D) The judge's discretion

Key Takeaway
Drawing lots in division is permissible and recommended; it assigns pre-existing shares, not new ones.

Refuting the Charge of Gambling and the Qiyas/Istihsan Contradiction
Defense of drawing lots against gambling charge and note on istihsan/qiyas contradiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi refutation of the claim that drawing lots is gambling, and identify the apparent contradiction between istihsan and qiyas in the Hanafi justification.

Core Idea
Hanafis defend qur'ah by distinguishing pre-existing entitlement from chance-created rights, and note a tension between istihsan and qiyas that can be resolved by understanding the level of analogy.

This lesson examines the critical part of the passage where the author defends drawing lots against the accusation of gambling. It also highlights an internal Hanafi debate: whether the permissibility of qur'ah is based on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas (analogy), or whether qiyas itself supports it. This refinement sharpens our understanding of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection is that linking entitlement to a random draw is gambling, which is haram. This is a potential counter-argument.
The objector assumes any chance-based allocation is qimar.
2
Understand the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes: in division, ownership already exists; the lot only assigns specific portions. This is not qimar because one does not gain what one had no right to.
The Quranic stories of Yunus and Zakariyya are cited as proof that lots are legislated.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The Quranic verses show that prophets used lots in similar situations, establishing that it is not prohibited.
Thubut (transmission) and dalala (meaning) are both qati (definitive).
4
Examine the apparent contradiction
The text notes that earlier it was said the method is based on istihsan (because qiyas analogizes it to gambling), but later it is argued that qiyas also supports it. This seems contradictory.
The author leaves this unresolved, but it indicates that the ruling is sound from both angles.
5
Resolve the contradiction
The claim that qiyas 'abstains' may refer to a superficial analogy; a deeper qiyas considering the underlying cause (illa) of fairness and necessity supports it.
Thus, there is no real contradiction; istihsan and qiyas align once the correct illa is identified.

قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared cause.

Inclusion of Dirhams in Division and Compensation for Buildings
Ruling on when cash can be included in division and compensation for building values

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on including dirhams in real estate division and identify the two views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding building compensation.

Core Idea
Dirhams cannot enter division without consent, but necessity allows cash to balance building values.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses when cash can be used to balance shares in a real estate division. The general rule is strict: dirhams are not included unless all partners agree, because cash creates inequality and risk. However, when land and building are divided, the school offers two ways to achieve equity: one by valuation and cash payment, another by land exchange, with cash only as a last resort.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the core principle: dirhams (cash) are not included in division except by mutual consent of all partners.
This is the default rule from the text.
2
Understand the rationale
Explain why cash is restricted: it creates inequality (one gets actual property, the other a debt) and carries risk of default.
The text says 'يفوت به التعديل في القسمة' – equity is lost.
3
Identify the exception for buildings
Recognize that land with a building requires special treatment. Two Hanafi opinions are given: Abu Yusuf divides by value and uses cash for compensation; Muhammad gives land equal to building value, using cash only if land is insufficient.
Both views allow cash out of necessity.
4
Follow the analogy
Note the analogy to the brother who has no authority over property but can name a dowry out of necessity for marriage validity. This justifies using cash when necessary.
Qiyas with the brother case shows necessity overrides the general prohibition.
5
Apply the rule
Practice applying the rule: given a scenario with partners and a building, determine when cash is permitted and which opinion applies.
Consider consent vs. necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا تدخل في القسمة الدراهم إلا برضاهم) يعني جماعة في أيديهم عقار فطلبوا القسمة وفي أحد الجانبين فضل عن الآخر فأراد أحدهم أن يدفع عوضه من الدراهم والآخر لم يرض بذلك لم تدخل الدراهم في القسمة لأنه لا شريك له فيها ويفوت به التعديل في القسمة لأن بعضهم يصل إلى عين المال المشترك في الحال ودراهم الآخر في الذمة فيخشى عليها التوى، وإذا كان أرض وبناء فعن الثاني أنه يقسم باعتبار القيمة لأنه يمكن اعتبار التعديل فيه إلا بالتقويم لأن تعديل البناء لا يمكن إلا بالمساحة والمساحة هي الأصل الممسوحات، ثم يرد من وقع البناء في نصيبه قيمة البناء أو من كان أجود دراهم على الآخر فتدخل الدراهم في القسمة ضرورة كالأخ لا ولاية له في المال ثم يملك تسمية الصداق ضرورة صحة التزويج. وعن محمد أنه يرد على شريكه بمقابلة البناء ما يساويه من العرصة، وإذا بقي فضل ولم يمكن تحقيق التسوية فيه بأن لم تف العرصة بقيمة البناء فحينئذ ترد الدارهم لأن الضرورة في هذا القدر فلا يترك الأصل وهو القسمة بالمساحة إلا
He (the author) said: (And dirhams are not included in division except by their consent). This means a group who have real estate and ask for division, and one side has an excess over the other, and one wants to give its compensation in dirhams but the other does not agree, dirhams are not included because he has no share in them and it ruins equitable division because some get the actual common property immediately while the other gets dirhams as a debt, which is subject to risk. And if there is land and building, from al-Thani (Abu Yusuf) that it is divided by value because equity can only be achieved by evaluation, since adjusting the building can only be by area, and area is the original measured quantity. Then the one in whose share the building falls pays the value of the building or the one with better dirhams pays the other, so dirhams enter the division out of necessity, like the brother who has no authority over property then owns the naming of dowry out of necessity for validity of marriage. And from Muhammad that he gives his partner in exchange for the building an equal amount of land. If there remains excess and equity cannot be achieved because the land does not cover the building's value, then dirhams are entered because of necessity to that extent, and the original principle (division by area) is not abandoned except [as needed].
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage deals with the use of cash to balance shares in real estate division. The principle: dirhams (currency) are not introduced into the division unless all parties consent, because it creates an inequity (one gets actual property, the other gets a promise of cash). However, when dividing land with buildings, there are different views. Abu Yusuf (al-Thani) holds that the division should be based on value, not just area, because the building's value cannot be equalized by area alone. So the one who gets the building in his share must compensate the other in cash. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the partner should receive land equivalent to the building's value. If the land is insufficient, then cash is used to the extent needed. Both opinions allow cash as a necessity to achieve fairness. The text mentions an analogy: the brother who has no authority over property can still name a dowry out of necessity for marriage validity.

Key Terms
دراهم (darahim): Dirhams (silver coins) representing cash payment used to balance shares in division.
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property among partners.
عقار (aqar): Real estate, immovable property.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits something otherwise prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition can dirhams be included in division without the consent of all partners?
A) When the property is arable land.
B) When one partner is a minor.
C) When dividing a building on land and achieving equity requires it.
D) When the judge orders it.

Key Takeaway
Dirhams are generally excluded from real estate division without consent, but necessity arising from building values permits cash compensation to achieve fairness.

Ruling on a Right of Way in Partition: Diversion or Void
Ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary on separating rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a co-owner has a path or watercourse in the other's share during partition and apply the condition that diversion must be attempted before voiding the partition.

Core Idea
A partition is void if a remaining right of way cannot be diverted — complete separation is its purpose.

Partition of jointly owned property aims to give each co-owner exclusive benefit. But what if one retains a right to pass through the other's land? The Hanafi school has a clear rule: the right must be diverted if possible; if not, the entire partition is void. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its rationale, and why it differs from a simple sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the problem
Recognize that the subject is 'partition' (qisma) of jointly owned property. The problem: one co-owner has a right of way (path or watercourse) in the share allotted to the other.
The right was not stipulated in the partition agreement.
2
Apply the condition: diversion first
The matn says: 'صرف عنه إن أمكن' — divert the right from the other's share if possible. This means the partition can stand if a new path or watercourse can be arranged for the right-holder without encroaching on the other's exclusive share.
Diversion must be physically and legally feasible.
3
Understand the 'illa: purpose of partition
The commentary gives the rationale: 'المقصود من القسمة تكميل المنفعة باختصاص كل بنصيبه وقطع أسباب تعلق حق الغير' — the purpose is complete benefit through exclusive ownership and severance of the other's rights. If a right remains, the purpose is defeated.
This is a qiyas based on the intent of the contract.
4
Contrast with sale
In a sale, lack of immediate access does not void the contract because the goal is transfer of ownership (ownership of the substance), not immediate use. Partition is different: its goal is immediate separation of use and ownership.
This distinction justifies the different ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة
طريق في ملك الآخر لم يشترط في القسمة صرف عنه إن أمكن وإلا فسخت القسمة هذا بالضرورة، وهذا يوافق رواية الأصل. وفي المحيط : ولو رفع القسمة على أن يزيد أحدهما شيئاً معلوماً فلا يخلو إما أن يكون المشروط دراهم أو دنانير أو مكيلاً أو موزوناً أو عروضاً أو حيواناً، فإن كان المشروط دراهم معلومة جاز بأن كانت مشروطة لتعديل الأنصباء فيجوز بالتراضي، وإن كانت الزيادة مشروطة لتقع القسمة على المفاضلة فيكون بيعاً من كل وجه وهو جائز بتراضيهما، وإن كانت الزيادة مكيلاً أو موزوناً ولم يسم مكان الإيفاء لم تجز عند الإمام، وعندهما تجوز ويسلمها عند الدار كما في السلم وإن كانت الزيادة عرضاً يجوز السلم فيها كالثوب جاز مؤجلاً ولا يجوز حالاً، وإن كان عروضاً لا يجوز السلم فيه، وإن كان حيواناً بعينه جاز، وبغير عينه لا يجوز . ثلاثة بينهم دور صغرى وكبرى فأخذ أحدهم الكبرى على أن يرد على الآخرين دراهم مسماة جاز، وكذلك لو أخذ الكبرى بنصيبين والصغرى بنصيب جاز. ولو اقتسموا الباب على أن من أصابه هذا رد درهماً، ومن أصابه رد در همین جاز. ولو اقتسموا الأراضي على أن من أصابه شجر ونبت في أرضه فعليه بقيمته دراهم جاز، ولو اقتسما على أن لأحدهما الصامت وللآخر العروض والنحاس والدين على أنه إن بقي عليه شيء من الدين يرد عليه نصفه فالقسمة فاسدة اهـ . قال رحمه الله : (وإن قسم ولأحدهم مسيل أو طريق في ملك الآخر لم يشترط في القسمة صرف عنه إن أمكن وإلا فسخت القسمة) لأن المقصود من القسمة تكميل المنفعة باختصاص كل بنصيبه وقطع أسباب تعلق حق الغير فإذا أمكن حصل المقصود وإلا لم يحصل فتعين الفسخ والاستئناف لنفي ضرر الاختلاط بخلاف البيع حيث لا يفسخ ولا يفسد فيما إذا لم يتمكن المشتري من الاستطراق ومن مسيل الطريق الماء لأن المقصود ملك الرقبة ولا يشترط فيه الانتفاع في الحال ولا كذلك القسمة. ولو ذكر الحقوق في الوجه الأول وهو ما إذا أمكن صرفه عن الآخر بأن قال هذا لك بحقوقه كان الجواب فيه مثل ما إذا لم يقل بحقوقه فيصرف عنه إن أمكن كما تقدم إلا إذا قال خذ هذا بطريقه وشربه ومسيله فحينئذ لا يصرف عنه لأنه أثبت له بأبلغ وجوه الإثبات بخلاف البيع إذا ذكر فيه الحقوق حيث يدخل فيه ما كان من الطريق والمسيل فيدخل عند التنصيص. واختلفوا في إدخال الطريق في القسمة بأن قال بعضهم لا يقسم الطريق بل يبقى مشتركاً مثل ما كان قبل القسمة ينظر فيه الحاكم؛ فإن كان يستقيم أن يفتح كل في نصيبه قسم الحاكم من غير طريق يرفع الجماعتهم تكميلا للمنفعة وتحقيقاً للإقرار من كل وجه، وإن كان لا يستقيم ذلك رفع طريقاً بين جماعتهم لتحقق تكميل المنفعة فيما وراء الطريق. ولو اختلفوا في مقدار عرضه يجعل على قدر عرض الباب بطوله أي ارتفاعه حتى يخرج كل واحد جناحاً في نصيبه إن كان فوق الباب لا فيما دونه لأن باب الدار طريق متفق عليه والمختلف فيه يرد إلى المتفق عليه، وفي هذا القدر كفاية في الدخول. ولو شرطوا أن يكون الطريق في الدار على التفاوت جاز وإن سهامهم في الدار متساوية لأن القسمة على التفاوت بالتراضي في غير الأموال الربوية جائزة، وإن كان ذلك أرضاً يرفع قدر ما يمر به نور لوقوع الكفاية به في المرور. ولم يذكر حكمه فيما إذا لم يكن له طريق وفي المحيط : ولو اقتسموا داراً فإذا لا طريق لأحدهم وقدر على أن يفتح في نصيبه طريقاً يمر فيه الرجل دون الحمولة جازت القسمة لأنها لم تتضمن تفويت منفعة، وإن لم يقدر ؛ ينظر إن لم يعلم أنه لا طريق له فالقسمة فاسدة، وإن علم أنه لا طريق له جازت القسمة لأنه رضي بهذه القسمة. دار في سكة غير نافذة اقتسموها على أن يفتح كل واحد باباً إلى السكة جاز ولا يمنعون منه لأنهم تصرفوا في خالص حقهم وهو الجدار ولا ضرر على غيرهم في ذلك مقصورة بين قوم طريقها في دار الآخر فاقتسموها فليس لكل واحد أن يفتح باباً المقصورة إلى الدار، وإنما من لهم طريق على مقدار الباب ولا يكون لهم حق المرور فيما سوى الطريق، وإن كان بجنب المقصورة دار لهم وقعت في قسمة رجل فأراد أحدهم أن يجعل الطريق إلى داره في هذه المقصورة لم يكن له ذلك طريق مشترك بين جماعة ليس لواحد منهم أن يفتح باباً لدار أخرى لا حق لها في هذه الطريق. ولو اقتسموا قرية فأصاب أحدهم قراح والآخر كرم والآخر بيوت جاز بتراضيهم، وإذا اقتسما كرم وفيه عنب وثمر ينظر ؛ إن قالا على أن النصف لفلان بكل قليل وكثير وما فيه من الأعشاب والثمار فهي مقسومة وإلا فهي على الشركة بينهما. دار وفيها طريق لآخر لا يمنعها عن قسمتها ويترك طريقه على عرض الباب العظمى، فإن باعوا الدار والطريق برضاهم ضرب صاحب الدار على مثلي ثمن الطريق وصاحب الممر بثلث الثمن لأن الطريق بينهم أثلاثاً إذا لم يعلم قدر الأنصباء فيكون الثمن بينهم أثلاثاً، وكذا إذا كان رقبة الطريق لاثنين وللآخر حق المرور. ومن مات منهم وتعددت ورثته اعتبر حقه كحق واحد، وإن لم يعرف أن الدار ميراث بينهم فالطريق على عدد الرؤوس وقسمة الطريق على عدد الرؤوس . ولو كان فيها طريق من ناحية وطريق لآخر من ناحية أخرى يعزل لهما طريق واحدة والطريق الواحد يكفي للمرور ولو اقتسموا داراً وفيها كنيف شارع إلى الطريق أو لم يحسب في ذرع الدار لأن الظلة والكنيف ليس لهما حق القرار على طريق العامة بل مستحق النقض، ومستحق النقض كالمنقوض ولكنهما يقومان على من وقعا في حيزه، ولا يحسبان في ذرعان الدار بعد قسمه الوالي وترك طريقاً للعامة فرأى الوالي بعد ذلك أن يعطي الطريق لواحد فينتفع بها ولا يضر بأهل الطريق جاز إن كانت المدينة له، وإن كانت للمسلمين لم يجز اهـ .
Book of Partition. A path in the ownership of the other not stipulated in the partition: it is diverted from him if possible; otherwise the partition is void. This is by necessity, and this agrees with the original narration. In al-Muhit: If they raise the partition upon one of them increasing something known, then it is either that the conditioned thing is dirhams or dinars or measured or weighed or goods or animals. If the conditioned thing is known dirhams, it is permissible, because it is conditioned to equalize the shares — it is permissible by mutual consent. If the increase is conditioned for the partition to occur upon difference, then it is a sale in every respect and it is permissible by their mutual consent. If the increase is measured or weighed and the place of delivery is not named, it is not permissible according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible and he delivers it at the house as in salam. If the increase is goods in which salam is permissible like a garment, it is permissible on credit and not permissible spot. If it is goods in which salam is not permissible, not permissible. If it is an animal in specie, permissible; not in specie, not permissible. Three persons: small and big houses among them. One takes the big one upon that he pays the others named dirhams — permissible. Likewise if he takes the big with two shares and the small with one share, permissible. And if they partition the door upon that whoever gets this pays a dirham, and whoever gets that pays a dirham — permissible. And if they partition lands upon that whoever gets trees and plants in his land owes its value in dirhams — permissible. And if they two partition upon that one gets the silver and gold and the other gets goods and copper and debt, upon that if anything of debt remains he returns half of it — the partition is void. End. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he partitioned and one of them has a watercourse or path in the ownership of the other not stipulated in the partition, it is diverted from him if possible; otherwise the partition is void) because the purpose of partition is completing the benefit by each being exclusive to his share and severing causes of attachment of the right of the other. So if possible, the purpose is achieved; otherwise not, so rescission and restart are determined to eliminate the harm of mixing, unlike sale where it is not rescinded nor invalidated when the buyer cannot access the road or watercourse, because the purpose is ownership of the substance and benefit at the moment is not required, unlike partition. And if the rights are mentioned in the first aspect, i.e., when it is possible to divert from the other, by saying 'this is yours with its rights', the answer is like when he did not say 'with its rights' — it is diverted from him if possible as previously, except if he says 'take this with its path, drinking place, and watercourse' — then it is not diverted from him because he has established it for him in the strongest manner of establishment, unlike sale when the rights are mentioned — where what is of path and watercourse enters, i.e., they enter when explicitly stated. And they differed about including the road in the partition. Some said: the road is not partitioned but remains shared as before partition; the judge looks: if it is feasible that each opens in his share, the judge partitions without a road to complete the benefit and achieve separation in every respect; if that is not feasible, he raises a road among them to achieve completion of benefit beyond the road. And if they differ about the width, it is made according to the width of the door in length (i.e., height) so that each brings out a side in his share if it is above the door, not below it, because the door of the house is a road agreed upon, and what is differed upon is referred to what is agreed upon. And this amount suffices for entry. And if they stipulate that the road in the house be differential, it is permissible even if their shares in the house are equal, because partition with difference by mutual consent in non-ribawi properties is permissible. If that is land, he raises the amount that light passes through for sufficiency in passing. And he did not mention its ruling when he has no road. In al-Muhit: If they partition a house and there is no road for one of them, and he is able to open in his share a road that a man can pass without load, the partition is permissible because it does not involve loss of benefit. If unable, it is considered: if he did not know that he has no road, the partition is void; if he knew he has no road, the partition is permissible because he is satisfied with this partition. A house in a blind alley; they partitioned it upon that each opens a door to the alley — permissible, and they are not prevented because they acted in their pure right which is the wall, and no harm to others. A qasura (pavilion) among people whose road is in another's house; they partitioned it: it is not for each to open a door from the qasura to the house. Rather, those who have a road have according to the measure of the door, and they have no right of passage beyond the road. If adjacent to the qasura is a house for them that fell in the partition of a man, and one of them wants to make the road to his house in this qasura, he does not have that. A shared road among a group: it is not for any one of them to open a door to another house that has no right in this road. And if they partition a village, and one gets a plot, another a vineyard, another houses — it is permissible by their mutual consent. And if they two partition a vineyard and there are grapes and fruit in it, it is considered: if they said it is for so-and-so with all little and much and what is in it of herbs and fruits, then it is partitioned; otherwise, it is on partnership between them. A house in which there is a road for another: he does not prevent its partition, and he leaves his road on the width of the largest door. If they sell the house and road with their consent, the owner of the house gets two-thirds of the price of the road, and the owner of the pass gets one-third, because the road among them is thirds when the amount of shares is unknown. Thus the price is among them in thirds. Likewise if the substance of the road belongs to two and the other has the right of passage. And if one of them dies and his heirs multiply, his right is considered as one right. If it is not known that the house is inheritance among them, the road is according to the number of heads, and partition of the road is according to the number of heads. And if in it is a road from one side and a road for another from another side, one road is assigned for them, and one road suffices for passage. And if they partition a house and in it is a lavatory projecting into the road or a canopy, it is not counted in the measurement of the house because the canopy and lavatory have no right of settlement on the public road; rather they are subject to demolition, and subject to demolition is like demolished. But they are valued for the one in whose space they fall, and they are not counted in the measurement of the house after the governor's partition, and he left a road for the public. Then the governor later decided to give the road to one person so that he benefits from it without harming the people of the road — it is permissible if the city belongs to him; if it belongs to the Muslims, it is not permissible. End.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a right of way (path or watercourse) that one partner has in the other partner's share after partition. The matn states that if during partition one co-owner has a right of way in the other's share, and this right was not stipulated in the partition agreement, then the right should be diverted (i.e., transferred away from the other's share) if possible. If diversion is not possible, the partition is void and must be redone. The commentary explains the rationale: the purpose of partition is to complete the benefit by granting each partner exclusive possession of his share and eliminating all mutual rights. If a right of way remains, the shares are not fully separated, defeating the purpose. This differs from a sale, where a buyer may purchase property without immediate access because the goal is ownership of the substance, not immediate use. The commentary then elaborates on various scenarios: If the partition includes financial compensation to adjust shares, the ruling depends on whether the compensation is dirhams, measured items, goods, etc. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa does not permit compensation in measured or weighed items without specifying the place of delivery, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit it, analogizing to salam. The text also covers cases where the path is explicitly mentioned, where the parties disagree on width, cases of dead-end alleys, multiple heirs, and partition of villages and vineyards. The overall message is that the primary goal of partition is complete separation of ownership and use; any lingering mutual rights undermine the partition and must be resolved, either by diversion or by voiding the partition.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Partition of jointly owned property into separate shares.
مسيل (masīl): A watercourse or channel for water flow.
طريق (ṭarīq): A path or right of way for passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi partition, if one co-owner has a right of way through the other's property and this was not stipulated, what happens?
A) The partition is always void.
B) The right of way is automatically cancelled.
C) The right of way is diverted from the other's share if possible; otherwise the partition is void.
D) The partition is valid, and the right of way remains.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi partition law, any undiverted right of way that cannot be relocated voids the partition because the purpose of partition is complete separation of ownership and use.
